Mut'ah: Conditions of Obligation and Recommendation
Expounds the conditions for recommended vs obligatory mut'ah in case of divorce before consummation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between obligatory and recommended mut'ah in Hanafi fiqh and identify the condition that determines each.

Core Idea
Mut'ah is wajib only when divorce occurs before consummation and no dower was specified; otherwise it is mustahabb or not due.

In this passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, the commentator clarifies the four scenarios of mut'ah after divorce. The ruling hinges on two factors: whether consummation occurred and whether a dower was specified. Understanding these distinctions is essential for applying the correct ruling in marriage and divorce cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios of divorce before consummation
The text outlines cases based on dower specification and consummation. List them.
The scenarios are: (1) consummation + dower specified, (2) consummation + no dower, (3) no consummation + dower specified, (4) no consummation + no dower.
2
Determine the mut'ah ruling for each scenario
From the text, identify whether mut'ah is obligatory, recommended, or not due in each case.
Mut'ah is mustahabb in cases 1 and 2; not due in case 3; wajib in case 4.
3
Examine the legal reasoning for the obligation in case 4
The text provides a dalil from Qur'an 4:24. Understand how the verse indicates that seeking the vulva requires wealth.
The word 'tabtaghu' and 'bi-amwalikum' imply that marriage involves financial compensation.
4
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The Hanafi position is that mut'ah is only wajib in case 4, whereas Shafi'i holds it wajib in all divorces before consummation. Note the practical difference.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf based on interpretation of the same verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالحاصل : أنه إذا وَطِئَها تستحب لها المتعة، سواءٌ سُمَّى لها مهرٌ أو لا ؛ لأنه أَوْحَشَهَا بالطلاق بعدما سَلَّمَت إليه المعقود عليه : وهو البضع ، فيستحب أن يعطيها شيئاً زائداً على الواجب : وهو المسمى في صورةِ التّسمية، ومهر المثل في صورة عدمِ التسمية. صورة فساد التسمية إنّما تجب المتعة إذا كان فسادها من كلِّ وجه، وإلا فإن صحت من وجه دون وجه لا تجب المتعة، وإن وجب مهر المثل بالدخول. كما إذا تزوجها على ألف درهم وكرامتها، أو على ألف وأن يهدي لها هدية ، فإذا طلقها قبل الدخول كان لها نصفُ الألف لا المتعة مع أنه لو دخل بها وجب مهر المثل لا ينقص عن الألف ؛ لأن المسمّى لم يفسد من كل وجه ؛ لأنه على تقدير كرامتها والإهداء يجب الألف لا مهر المثل. كذا في غاية البيان» و«البحر الرائق». [١) قوله : فالحاصل ؛ أي حاصل أحكام الصور الأربع : أن استحباب المتعة مختص بصورة كونها موطوءة سواء كان المهر مسمى أو لا ، فإن كان المهر مسمَّى يجب كماله، وإن لم يكن مسمّى يجب مهر المثل، وتستحب المتعة في الصورتين، ووجوب المتعة بصورة عدم الوطء وعدم التسمية، وعدم استحبابها ووجوبها مختص بصورة وجود التسمية وعدم الوطء. [٢] قوله : لأنه ... الخ ؛ بيان أمرِ شرعيّة المتعة ، وهو لَمَّا طلقها بعدما أخذ منافع بضعها أدخل الوحشة عليها بفراقها ، فينبغي أن يعطيها شيئاً زائداً على قدر الواجب إدخالاً للسرور والنشاط عليها وجبراً لِمَا فات منها. [۳] قوله : سلّمت ؛ أي بعد تسليمها المعقود عليه، وهو منافع البضع. [٤] قوله : وهو ؛ أي الواجب إعطاء المهر المقدر في صورة كونه مقداراً، ومهر المثل في صورة عدم كونه مقدراً.
 وإن قبضت ألفاً سُمِّي لها ، ثمَّ وهبتُه ،له ، وطلّقت قبل وطءٍ رَجَعَ عليها بنصفه وإن لم يطأها : ففي صورة التّسميَّةِ تأخذ نصف المسمّى من غير تسمية البضع ، ولا يستحب لها شيء آخر. وفي صورة عدم التسمية تجب المتعة ؛ لأنها لم تأخذ شيئاً، وابتغاء البضع لا ينفك عن المال. (وإن قبضت ألفاً سُمِّي لها ، ثمّ وهبته له ، وطُلقت قبل وطءٍ رَجَعَ عليها بنصفه) [١] قوله : ففي صورة التسمية ؛ يعني إذا سمى لها مهراً وطلقها قبل أن يأخذ منافع البضع الواجب عليه أداء نصف المسمى بالنص القرآني ، ولم يوجد هاهنا الإيحاش بعد تسليم البضع ؛ ليستحب إعطاء شيءٍ زائد لها على الواجب ؛ فلذلك لا تستحب المتعة في هذه الصورة. [٢) قوله : وفي صورة عدم التسمية ؛ يعني إذا طلقها ولم يسم لها مهراً ولم يطأها تجب المتعة ؛ لأنه لا سبيل إلى وجوب نصف المهرِ ؛ إذ لا تسمية هاهنا، ولا إلى وجوب مهر المثل، فإن وجوبه إنما يكون بالموتِ أو بالوطء، ولا إلى وجوب نصف مهر المثل ؛ لأن التنصيف مختص بالمهر المسمى، ومهر المثل لا يتنصف شرعاً. ولا سبيل أيضاً إلى عدم وجوب شيء، فإنّ ابتغاء البضع ملصق بالمالِ شرعاً ؛ لقوله عملة : ﴿ وَأُحِلَّ لَكُم مَّا وَرَاة ذَلِكُمْ أَن تَبْتَغُوا بِأَمْوَالِكُم ﴾، فلذلك وجبت المتعة في هذه الصورة. [٣] قوله : وإن قبضت ... الخ ؛ يعني إذا نكح امرأة على ألف وأعطى كله، فقبضته ثم وهبت المرأة الألف لزوجها ، ثم طلقها ولم يطأها رجع الزوج عليها بنصف الألف. [٤]قوله : رجع ؛ أي أخذ الزوج منها نصفُ الذي أعطاه، وهو الألف ولا يقدح فيه هبتها الألف.
The summary: When he has intercourse with her, it is recommended (mustahabb) for her to receive a gift (mut'ah), whether a dower (mahr) was specified for her or not; because he has caused her distress by divorce after she has surrendered to him the object of the contract, which is the vulva (al-bid'), so it is recommended that he give her something extra beyond what is obligatory, which is the specified dower in the case of specification, and the dower of the like (mahr al-mithl) in the case of no specification. The case of an invalid specification: mut'ah is only obligatory if the invalidity is from every aspect; otherwise, if it is valid from one aspect but not another, mut'ah is not obligatory, even if mahr al-mithl becomes obligatory by consummation. For example, if he marries her for one thousand dirhams and her dignity (karamatiha), or for one thousand and that he give her a gift, then if he divorces her before consummation, she gets half of the thousand, not mut'ah, even though if he had consummated, mahr al-mithl would be obligatory not less than the thousand; because the specified dower is not invalid from every aspect; because on the basis of her dignity and the gift, the thousand is obligatory, not mahr al-mithl. Thus in Ghayat al-Bayan and al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. [1] The commentator says: 'The summary' means the summary of the rulings of the four cases: that the recommendation of mut'ah is specific to the case where she is cohabited (mawtu'a), whether a dower is specified or not. If the dower is specified, its full amount is obligatory; if not specified, mahr al-mithl is obligatory, and mut'ah is recommended in both cases. The obligation of mut'ah applies to the case of no cohabitation and no specification, while its non-recommendation and non-obligation is specific to the case where there is specification and no cohabitation. [2] His saying: 'because...' etc. is an explanation of the legal nature of mut'ah: that when he divorces her after taking the benefits of her vulva, he has brought distress upon her by separation, so he should give her something extra beyond what is obligatory, to bring joy and cheer to her and to compensate for what she missed. [3] His saying: 'surrendered' means after she has surrendered the object of the contract, which is the benefits of the vulva. [4] His saying: 'which is' means the obligatory giving of the fixed dower in case it is fixed, and mahr al-mithl in case it is not fixed.
And if she received a thousand that was specified for her, then she gave it to him as a gift, and she is divorced before cohabitation, he takes back half of it. And if he does not cohabit with her: In the case of specification, she takes half of the specified dower without any gift for the vulva, and nothing else is recommended for her. In the case of no specification, mut'ah is obligatory; because she has taken nothing, and seeking the vulva is not free from wealth. (And if she received a thousand specified for her, then she gave it to him as a gift, and she is divorced before cohabitation, he takes back half of it) [1] His saying: 'In the case of specification' means that if he specified a dower for her and divorces her before taking the benefits of the vulva, it is obligatory upon him to pay half of the specified dower by the Qur'anic text, and there is no cause of distress after surrendering the vulba to make it recommended to give extra; therefore mut'ah is not recommended in this case. [2] His saying: 'And in the case of no specification' means that if he divorces her without specifying a dower and without cohabiting with her, mut'ah is obligatory; because there is no way to obligate half the dower (since there is no specification here), nor to obligate mahr al-mithl (since its obligation is only by death or cohabitation), nor to obligate half of mahr al-mithl (because division into half is specific to the specified dower, and mahr al-mithl is not halved legally). Nor is there a way to not obligate anything, because seeking the vulva is legally attached to wealth; due to His saying: {... that you seek with your wealth} (Qur'an 4:24). Therefore mut'ah became obligatory in this case. [3] His saying: 'And if she received...' etc. means that if he married a woman for one thousand and gave it all, and she received it, then the woman gave the thousand as a gift to her husband, then he divorced her without cohabiting, the husband takes back half of the thousand. [4] His saying: 'takes back' means the husband takes from her half of what he gave, which is the thousand; her gifting of the thousand does not impair this.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, details the rulings of mut'ah (a compensatory gift) for a woman divorced before consummation. The passage type is a detailed expansion of the legal rules. The author first summarizes that mut'ah is recommended (mustahabb) when divorce occurs after the husband has had intercourse with his wife, regardless of whether a dower (mahr) was specified. The reason given is jurisprudential: the husband has benefited from her vulva (bida') and then separated from her, causing her distress, so he should give her extra beyond the obligatory dower to console her. This extra is the mut'ah. The obligatory dower is either the specified amount (mahr musamma) or the dower of the like (mahr al-mithl) if none was specified. Next, the text addresses a scenario where the dower specification is partially invalid, e.g., marrying 'on one thousand and her dignity' or 'on one thousand and a gift'. Here, if divorce occurs before consummation, she gets half of the thousand but no mut'ah, because the specification is valid in part. If consummation occurred, she would get mahr al-mithl not less than the thousand. This shows that mut'ah is only obligatory if the specification is invalid entirely (fasad min kulli wajh); if partially valid, no mut'ah. The passage then moves to the case where the wife has received the specified dower and then gifts it back to her husband, followed by divorce before consummation. The husband takes back half of the dower from her. This is because the gift does not affect the legal obligation: she still owes half upon divorce. Finally, the commentator clarifies two subcases: when a dower is specified and no consummation, she takes half the dower and no mut'ah is recommended, because the distress is absent. When no dower was specified and no consummation, mut'ah is obligatory, supported by Qur'an 4:24, which indicates that seeking marriage involves wealth. So mut'ah compensates for the lack of any dower. The Hanafi position is clear: mut'ah is recommended after consummation, obligatory without dower and before consummation, and not recommended when a dower is specified and no consummation.

Key Terms
متعة (mut'ah): A compensatory gift given by the husband to the wife upon divorce, consisting of money or goods, to console her for the distress of separation.
بضع (bida'): The vulva; legally, it refers to the subject matter of the marriage contract—the wife's sexual organ, which the husband has the right to enjoy.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of the like; the amount of dower appropriate for a woman similar to the wife in status, family, beauty, etc., when no dower was specified in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi madhhab, when is mut'ah (compensatory gift) obligatory upon divorce before consummation?
A) When a dower was specified and the husband had intercourse.
B) When no dower was specified and no intercourse occurred.
C) Only when the dower was invalid from every aspect.
D) Whenever the divorce is initiated by the husband.

Key Takeaway
Mut'ah is obligatory (wajib) only in the absence of both a dower and consummation; otherwise it is recommended or not due.

Mut'ah: Invalid Dower Specification and Gift-Back Cases
Expounds the conditions for mut'ah when dower specification is partially invalid and the effect of the wife gifting back the dower.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the ruling on mut'ah when the dower specification is partially invalid and determine the effect of a wife gifting back the dower on the husband's right to reclaim half.

Core Idea
When a dower specification is partially valid, mut'ah is not due; half the dower is paid. Gifting back the dower does not prevent the husband from reclaiming half upon divorce before consummation.

This lesson examines two specific scenarios from the same passage: the case of a partially invalid dower (like marrying for a sum plus her dignity) and the case where the wife gifts the entire dower back to her husband and then gets divorced before consummation. These cases clarify the boundaries of mut'ah obligation and the effect of gifts on financial rights.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition for mut'ah in invalid dower cases
The text states that mut'ah is wajib only if the invalidity is from every aspect. If partially valid, no mut'ah. Identify an example.
Example: marriage for 1000 and her dignity; the 1000 is valid.
2
Trace the ruling for partially invalid specification
The wife gets half the valid portion (1000 dirhams) and no mut'ah, because the valid part establishes a dower.
This differs from the fully invalid case where mut'ah becomes wajib.
3
Analyze the gift-back scenario
If the wife receives the dower and then gifts it back, then divorce occurs before consummation, the husband takes back half. Why?
The gift does not extinguish her obligation to return half upon divorce.
4
Apply these rules to derive the financial outcome
Calculate what each party receives in the gift-back case.
Wife originally had 1000, she gave it back, then husband takes 500 from her assets.

In the case of no specification, mut'ah is obligatory; because she has taken nothing, and seeking the vulva is not free from wealth. (And if she received a thousand specified for her, then she gave it to him as a gift, and she is divorced before cohabitation, he takes back half of it) [1] His saying: 'In the case of specification' means that if he specified a dower for her and divorces her before taking the benefits of the vulva, it is obligatory upon him to pay half of the specified dower by the Qur'anic text, and there is no cause of distress after surrendering the vulba to make it recommended to give extra; therefore mut'ah is not recommended in this case. [2] His saying: 'And in the case of no specification' means that if he divorces her without specifying a dower and without cohabiting with her, mut'ah is obligatory; because there is no way to obligate half the dower (since there is no specification here), nor to obligate mahr al-mithl (since its obligation is only by death or cohabitation), nor to obligate half of mahr al-mithl (because division into half is specific to the specified dower, and mahr al-mithl is not halved legally). Nor is there a way to not obligate anything, because seeking the vulva is legally attached to wealth; due to His saying: {... that you seek with your wealth} (Qur'an 4:24). Therefore mut'ah became obligatory in this case. [3] His saying: 'And if she received...' etc. means that if he married a woman for one thousand and gave it all, and she received it, then the woman gave the thousand as a gift to her husband, then he divorced her without cohabiting, the husband takes back half of the thousand. [4] His saying: 'takes back' means the husband takes from her half of what he gave, which is the thousand; her gifting of the thousand does not impair this.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, details the rulings of mut'ah (a compensatory gift) for a woman divorced before consummation. The passage type is a detailed expansion of the legal rules. The author first summarizes that mut'ah is recommended (mustahabb) when divorce occurs after the husband has had intercourse with his wife, regardless of whether a dower (mahr) was specified. The reason given is jurisprudential: the husband has benefited from her vulva (bida') and then separated from her, causing her distress, so he should give her extra beyond the obligatory dower to console her. This extra is the mut'ah. The obligatory dower is either the specified amount (mahr musamma) or the dower of the like (mahr al-mithl) if none was specified. Next, the text addresses a scenario where the dower specification is partially invalid, e.g., marrying 'on one thousand and her dignity' or 'on one thousand and a gift'. Here, if divorce occurs before consummation, she gets half of the thousand but no mut'ah, because the specification is valid in part. If consummation occurred, she would get mahr al-mithl not less than the thousand. This shows that mut'ah is only obligatory if the specification is invalid entirely (fasad min kulli wajh); if partially valid, no mut'ah. The passage then moves to the case where the wife has received the specified dower and then gifts it back to her husband, followed by divorce before consummation. The husband takes back half of the dower from her. This is because the gift does not affect the legal obligation: she still owes half upon divorce. Finally, the commentator clarifies two subcases: when a dower is specified and no consummation, she takes half the dower and no mut'ah is recommended, because the distress is absent. When no dower was specified and no consummation, mut'ah is obligatory, supported by Qur'an 4:24, which indicates that seeking marriage involves wealth. So mut'ah compensates for the lack of any dower. The Hanafi position is clear: mut'ah is recommended after consummation, obligatory without dower and before consummation, and not recommended when a dower is specified and no consummation.

Key Terms
متعة (mut'ah): A compensatory gift given by the husband to the wife upon divorce, consisting of money or goods, to console her for the distress of separation.
بضع (bida'): The vulva; legally, it refers to the subject matter of the marriage contract—the wife's sexual organ, which the husband has the right to enjoy.
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of the like; the amount of dower appropriate for a woman similar to the wife in status, family, beauty, etc., when no dower was specified in the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wife receives a dower of 5000 dirhams, gifts it back to her husband, and then he divorces her before consummation. How much does the husband take back from her?
A) 5000 dirhams
B) 2500 dirhams
C) 0 dirhams
D) 1250 dirhams

Key Takeaway
Gifting back the dower does not prevent the husband from reclaiming half upon divorce before consummation; the obligation to return half is independent.

Nikah — Marriage

Specified vs Unspecified Mahr: Half or Mut'ah?
Ruling with proof: two mahr scenarios and a detailed case of recovery after gift

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi rulings for divorce before consummation (specified vs unspecified mahr) and apply the principle that dirhams and dinars are fungible when a gift of the mahr is made.

Core Idea
If mahr was specified, wife gets half; if unspecified, mut'ah is wajib. Currency is not specific in recovery.

When a marriage ends by divorce before consummation, the financial obligations depend on whether a mahr (dower) was specified in the contract. This commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains two distinct scenarios and the reasoning behind them. Additionally, a practical case where the wife gifts back the mahr before divorce is analyzed, illustrating the Hanafi principle that dirhams and dinars are not considered specific property ('ayn) in transactions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine whether a mahr was specified in the marriage contract. The ruling differs fundamentally between these two cases.
The divorce must occur before consummation (and before valid seclusion) for these rules to apply.
2
Apply the rule for specified mahr
If a mahr was specified and the woman has not been touched, she is entitled to half of that specified amount. No additional mut'ah is recommended.
The Quranic basis is Surah al-Baqarah 2:237, which explicitly commands half when divorce occurs before consummation.
3
Apply the rule for unspecified mahr
If no mahr was specified, mut'ah (a compensation gift) becomes obligatory (wajib). The husband cannot be required to pay half of an unspecified mahr, nor full mahr al-mithl, but the marital bond inherently involves wealth.
The proof is Surah al-Nisa 4:24, which links seeking the vulva to wealth, implying compensation must be given.
4
Analyze the gift scenario
When the wife receives the full specified mahr, then gifts it back, and is divorced before consummation, the husband can reclaim half. Because the gift is considered a transfer of fungible currency, not the specific coins that were the mahr, his right to recover the excess (the half) remains intact.
This demonstrates the Hanafi principle 'al-darahim wa al-dananir la tata'ayyan' – dirhams and dinars are not specific in legal transactions.

[2] In the case of no specification, mut'ah is obligatory, because she did not receive anything, and seeking the vulva is not free from wealth. [3] (And if she received a thousand specified for her, then she gifted it to him, and she was divorced before intercourse, he recovers half of it from her.) [1] His statement: 'In the case of specification'; he means if he specified a mahr for her and divorced her before he took the benefits of the vulva which was obligatory upon him to pay half of the specified (mahr) by the Quranic text, and there is no cause for repulsion here after delivery of the vulva, so that giving something extra beyond what is obligatory would be recommended; therefore mut'ah is not recommended in this case. [2] His statement: 'And in the case of no specification'; he means if he divorced her and did not specify a mahr for her and did not have intercourse with her, mut'ah is obligatory; because there is no way to obligate half of the mahr—since there is no specification here—nor to obligate the mahr of the like (mahr al-mithl)—for its obligation is only by death or intercourse—nor to obligate half of the mahr of the like—because half is specific to the named mahr, and the mahr of the like is not halved legally. And there is also no way to not obligate anything, because seeking the vulva is attached to wealth legally; due to His (the Prophet's) statement: 'And lawful to you are what is beyond that, that you seek with your wealth' (Quran 4:24). Therefore mut'ah is obligatory in this case. [3] His statement: 'And if she received...' etc.; he means if a man married a woman for a thousand and gave it all, and she received it, then the woman gifted the thousand to her husband, then he divorced her before intercourse, the husband recovers half of the thousand from her. [4] His statement: 'he recovers'; i.e., the husband takes from her half of what he gave, which is the thousand, and her gifting of the thousand does not prevent that. Because she received the entire specified (mahr) while only half was obligatory, so she returns half, and the thousand which she gifted to him is not specifically identified as the mahr thousand; because dirhams and dinars are not specified in contracts and dissolutions. [1] His statement: 'so she returns the half'; i.e., half of the mahr she received. If you say: When he gave her all the mahr and she received it, her ownership of it was complete, and his right dropped, so what is the meaning of returning? I say: His giving the thousand was not by way of donation and gift, but by way of fulfilling her debt (the mahr). And when he divorced her before intercourse, it became known that her debt was only half of it, so what was additional is liable to be returned; because she only received it on the basis that it was her right, and he also gave on that basis. When it is proven that her right was to half of it, his right to reclaim half is established. If you say: It has passed that the obligation of the specified mahr is by the contract itself, then his giving the thousand is giving what was obligatory upon him, so he should not reclaim anything. I say: Yes, but that obligation at that time is suspended; if seclusion (khalwa) occurs afterwards, its obligation becomes confirmed; and if it does not occur and separation from him occurs before it, it halves. So in our case, when he divorced her before the confirmatory factor of full mahr, it became known that her right and what was obligatory upon him was only half, so he must necessarily reclaim what he paid in excess. [2] His statement: 'And the thousand...' etc.; it is a rebuttal of what might be said: How can his recovery be valid given that what he paid had already come back to him entirely—in the scenario of her gifting the entire thousand, or half in the scenario of her gifting half—for the assumption is that she gifted him what she had received, so his right has reached him. The gist of the rebuttal: The thousand she gifted to him is not specifically identified as the mahr thousand; because if she gifted an absolute thousand, the matter is obvious; and if she gifted that specific thousand she had taken, it is likewise, due to the non-specification of dirhams and dinars. In summary, the gift is attached to the thousand (as a quantity), so the actual object of his right has not reached him to cause his recovery to fall. [3] His statement: 'in contracts'; i.e., legal transactions such as sale and purchase; and 'dissolutions'; i.e., cancellation of transactions such as rescission of sale and similar. For example: if someone sold something for ten specific dirhams, it does not attach...
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn from the chapter of Mahr in Nikah. It explains two distinct rulings when divorce occurs before consummation. First, when a mahr was specified, the wife is entitled to half of that specified amount, and no additional mut'ah is recommended. The commentator explains that because the husband has not yet benefited from the marriage (no intercourse or valid seclusion), he only owes half the mahr by Quranic decree (Surah al-Baqarah 2:237). There is no cause for extra compensation. Second, when no mahr was specified, the wife is entitled to obligatory mut'ah (a gift of consolation). The commentator reasons that since no mahr was named, half the mahr cannot be given; mahr al-mithl (proper mahr) is only due upon death or actual intercourse; and it is not halved. Yet the woman is entitled to something because marriage involves seeking the vulva, which is linked to wealth by the Quran (4:24). Hence, mut'ah is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school in this case. The passage then addresses a scenario: a woman receives the full specified mahr (1000 dirhams), gifts it back to her husband, and is then divorced before consummation. The husband may reclaim half of the 1000 from her. The commentator explains that the husband gave the mahr as payment of a debt, not as a gift. The debt was not fully due; only half was due after divorce before consummation. Thus the excess is recoverable. Furthermore, the wife's gift of the thousand back to the husband does not prevent his recovery because dirhams and dinars are non-specific in contracts and dissolutions (they are fungible). The gift is considered a transfer of a quantity, not the specific coins that were the mahr. Therefore, the husband can still claim his half. The commentator addresses hypothetical objections: (1) Since ownership transferred to the wife when she received the mahr, how can the husband reclaim? Answer: The transfer was conditional on it being the full mahr; when it becomes clear only half was due, the excess remains recoverable. (2) The obligation was fixed at the contract, so why reclaim? Answer: The obligation is suspended pending consummation; divorce before consummation halves it. (3) Since she gifted back the very same amount, his right has been returned. Answer: The gift is of the quantity, not the specific coins, so his right to the original mahr money is not satisfied. This is a classic Hanafi application of the principle that dirhams and dinars are not 'ayn (specific) in transactions.

Key Terms
المتعة (al-mut'ah): A gift of consolation given to a divorced woman when no mahr was specified and no consummation occurred.
الدراهم والدنانير لا تتعين (al-darahim wa al-dananir la tata'ayyan): Dirhams and dinars are not considered specific ('ayn) in contracts and dissolutions; they are fungible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Half of mahr al-mithl
B) Mut'ah (a gift)
C) Full mahr al-mithl
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes two obligations upon divorce before consummation: half of specified mahr or wajib mut'ah if unspecified, with the principle that currency fungibility prevents gift cancellation of recovery.

When Wife Gifts Back Mahr and Divorce Before Consummation: The Fungibility Principle
Commentary on a ruling about mahr and gift before divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that dirhams and dinars are not specified in contracts to determine the wife's obligation to return half of the mahr when she gifts it back and is divorced before consummation.

Core Idea
A gift of fungible mahr does not discharge the half owed upon divorce before consummation.

This passage from a commentary on Al-Wiqayah addresses a nuanced scenario: the wife receives the full mahr, then gifts it back to her husband, after which he divorces her before consummation. At first glance, one might think the gift settles the matter, but the commentator clarifies that because dirhams and dinars are fungible and not specified in contracts, the gift does not transfer the specific coins owed. The husband still retains a right to reclaim the half that was never actually due. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning, including the key fungibility principle and an intra-Hanafi dispute over how much is returned when the wife received more than half.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario and the ruling
The matn rules that when the wife receives the full mahr and gifts it back, then is divorced before consummation, she must return half of what she received. Confirm the obligation and its basis.
The half returned is half of the named mahr, not half of the gift.
2
Understand the rationale: fungibility of dirhams and dinars
The commentator explains that dirhams and dinars are not specified in contracts (لا تتعين). When the husband gave the mahr, it was a payment of a debt; when the wife gifted it back, the gift did not specifically return the same coins, so the husband's right to recover the excess (half) remains.
This principle applies to all fungible goods (mithliyyat).
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on excess receipt
If the wife received more than half (e.g., 600 out of 1000) and gifted the remainder (400), Abu Hanifa holds she returns only the excess over half (100); the Sahibayn hold she returns half of what she received (300). Trace the reasoning: Abu Hanifa views the excess as never owed, so only that must be returned.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view per al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.
4
Apply the ruling to similar scenarios
Consider variations: if she received less than half, she owes nothing; if she sold the mahr item, the husband recovers half its value. The principle remains the same.
Non-fungible mahr (e.g., a specific house) would be treated differently.

Source Text

[١) قوله : فتردُّ النصف ؛ أي نصفُ المهر الذي قبضته. فإن قلت : لما أعطاها كلّ المهر وقبضته كمل ملكها فيه، وسقط حقه، فما معنى الرد؟
قلت : إعطاؤه الألف لم يكن على سبيل التبرع والهبة، بل على سبيل أداء دينها، وهو المهر ، ولَمَّا طلقها قبل الوطء عَلِمَ أن دينها لم يكن إلا نصفه، فكان ما زاد عليه مُسْتَحِق الردّ ؛ لأنها ما قبضته إلا على سبيل أنه حقها ، وهو أعطى أيضاً على هذا السبيل ، فلما ثبت أنّ حقها كان في نصفه ثبت له رجوع نصفه.
فإن قلت : قد مر أن وجوب المهر المسمى بنفس العقد فحينئذ يكون إعطاؤه الألف إعطاءً لِمَا وَجَبَ عليه ، فينبغي أن لا يرجع بشيء.
قلت : نعم ؛ لكن ذلك الواجب عند ذلك يكون موقوفاً حتى لو وجدت الخلوة بعده يتأكد وجوبه ، ولو لم يوجد وحصلت الفرقة منه قبلها يتنصف، ففيما نحن فيه لَمَّا طلقها قبل مؤكّد تمام المهر عَلِمَ أن حقها والواجب عليه لم يكن إلا النصف فلا بد أن يرجع ما أدّاه زائداً.
[٢] قوله : والألف ... الخ ؛ دفع لما يقال : إنه كيف يصح رجوعه، والحال أنه قد وصل إليه ما أدّاه كله . في صورة هبتها كلّ الألف ، أو نصفه في صورة هبته النصف، فإنّ المفروض أنها وهبته ذلك الذي قبضته، فقد وصل إليه حقه.
وحاصل الدفع : أن الألف الذي وهبته له لم يتعين كونه ألف المهر ؛ وذلك لأنه إن وهبت مطلق الألف، فالأمر ظاهر، وإن وهبت ذلك الألف الذي أخذته بعينه ، فكذلك لعدم تعين الدراهم والدنانير وبالجملة الهبة تعلقت بالألف ، فلم يصل إليه عين حقه حتى يسقط رجوعه. (۳) قوله : في العقود : أي المعاملات الشرعية: كالبيع والشراء، والفسوخ: أي فسخ المعاملات : كإقالة البيع ونحوه ، مثلاً : لو باع شيئاً بعشرة دراهم معيَّنةً لا يتعلق العقد بعينها حتى لو أداه المشتري غيرها أجزأه ، ولو فسخ البائع والمشتري البيع، ورد المشتري المبيع على البائع لا يجب على البائع ردُّ تلك الدراهم التي قبضها من المشتري بأعيانها ، بل ردُّ ما يماثلها أيضاً كاف.
وكذا الحكم في كلّ مكيل وموزون ، وأما الأعيان غير هذه الأشياء فتتعين في العقود والفسوخ كما تتعينُ هذه الأشياء في الغصوب والودائع ونحوها حتى لو غَصَبَ من رجل درهما يجب عليه ردّ عينه.
[1]قوله : وإن لم تقبضه ؛ أي ذلك الألف الذي سمي في العقد.
[٢] قوله: نصفه ؛ احتراز عما إذا قبضت أكثر من النصف، ثم وهبت كله وطلقت قبل الدخول، فإنّها تردُّ عليه ما زادَ على النصف، ولو قبضت الأقـل مـن النصف فوهبته ثم . طلقت قبل الدخول لا يرجع عليها بشيء. كذا في «البحر»). [٣] قوله : ثمّ وهبت الكلّ ؛ أي كلّ المهر المسمى هو الألف، هذا في الصورتين : أي صورة عدم قبض شيء منه، وصورة قبض النصف، ومعنى هبته الألف بعد قبض النصف أنها وهَبَتْ له المقبوض وغيره، فتخصيص هبة الكلِّ بالصورة الأولى كما صدر من مؤلّف «الدر المختار» مما لا وجه له.
[٤]قوله : أو ما بقي ؛ هذا مختص بالصورة الثانية : أي قبض النصف، بأن قبضت نصف مهرها وأبرأته عن باقيه، ولا وجود له في الصورة الأولى؛ لأن الباقي يقتضي قبض شيء، وإذ ليس فليس.
[0] قوله : أو وهبت ؛ أي كلّه أو أكثر من نصفه ولو وهبت أقل من نصف عَرَضِ المهر تردُّ ما زاد على النصف، ولو باعته من زوجها يرجع عليها بنصف قيمته.
(۱) قيد بقبض النصف للاحتراز عما إذا قبضت أكثر من النصف ووهبت الباقي، فإنها تَرُدُّ عليه ما زاد على النصف عنده كما لو قبضت ستمئة ووهبت أربعمئة فإنه يرجع بمئة وعندهما يرجعُ بنصف المقبوض فتَرُدُّ ثلاثمئة. ينظر : ((البحر الرائق»(۳: ۱۷۱).
Because she received the full dower while only half was obligatory, so she returns half, and the thousand she gifted to him is not specified as the dower thousand because dirhams and dinars are not specified in contracts and rescissions. [1] His statement: 'so she returns half' i.e., half of the dower she received. If it is said: When he gave her all the dower and she received it, her ownership of it is complete and his right is dropped, so what is the meaning of returning? I say: His giving the thousand was not as a gift or donation, but for payment of her debt, which is the dower. When he divorced her before intercourse, it became known that her debt was only half of it, so what exceeded that is entitled to be returned, because she received it only as her right, and he gave it also on this basis. So when it is established that her right was in half of it, his right to recover half is established. If it is said: It has passed that the obligation of the specified dower is by the contract itself, so then his giving the thousand is a giving of what was obligatory upon him, so he should not recover anything. I say: Yes, but that obligatory at that time is suspended. If consummation occurs afterwards, its obligation is confirmed. If it does not occur and separation from him occurs before it, it becomes half. So in our case, when he divorced her before the confirmation of the full dower, it became known that her right and what was obligatory upon him was only half, so he must recover what he paid in excess. [2] His statement: 'and the thousand...' etc., is a rebuttal to what is said: How can his recovery be valid while what he gave has reached him entirely? In the case of her gifting all the thousand, or half in the case of his gifting half, because it is assumed that she gifted him what she received, so his right has reached him. The summary of the rebuttal: The thousand she gifted to him is not specified as being the dower thousand, because if she gifted the absolute thousand, the matter is clear; and if she gifted that specific thousand she took, similarly due to the non-specification of dirhams and dinars. In short, the gift is attached to the thousand, so the very object of his right has not reached him such that his recovery is dropped. (3) His statement: 'in contracts' i.e., legal transactions like sale and purchase, and rescissions: i.e., cancellation of transactions like revocation of sale and the like. For example, if someone sold something for ten specific dirhams, the contract does not attach to those specific dirhams, so even if the buyer pays other dirhams, it suffices. And if the seller and buyer rescind the sale and the buyer returns the item to the seller, the seller is not obliged to return those specific dirhams he took from the buyer, but returning their equivalent is also sufficient. Similarly, the ruling applies to every weighed or measured item. As for non-fungible items, they are specified in contracts and rescissions just as these items are specified in usurpations, deposits, and the like, such that if someone usurps a dirham from a man, he must return that specific dirham. [1] His statement: 'And if she did not receive it' i.e., that thousand named in the contract. [2] His statement: 'half of it' is a qualification for the case where she received more than half, then gifted it all and was divorced before consummation, then she returns to him the excess over half. If she received less than half and gifted it, then was divorced before consummation, he does not recover anything from her. This is in al-Bahr. [3] His statement: 'then gave all' i.e., all the named dower which is the thousand. This applies to both cases: the case of not receiving anything of it and the case of receiving half. The meaning of her gifting the thousand after receiving half is that she gifted to him what she received and other than it. So specifying the gift of all to the first case, as done by the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar, has no basis. [4] His statement: 'or what remains' is specific to the second case, i.e., receiving half, in that she received half of her dower and released him from the remainder. It does not exist in the first case because 'remainder' implies receiving something, and there is none. [0] His statement: 'or she gave' i.e., all or more than half of it. If she gave less than half of the dower (if it is a commodity), she returns the excess over half. If she sold it to her husband, he recovers from her half of its value. (1) The qualification by receiving half is to guard against the case where she received more than half and gifted the remainder. In that case, she returns to him the excess over half according to him—as if she received six hundred and gifted four hundred, then he recovers one hundred—while according to them, he recovers half of what was received, so she returns three hundred. See al-Bahr al-Ra'iq 3:171.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) expanding on a ruling from the matn of Al-Wiqayah regarding the consequences when a wife, after receiving the full dower (mahr), gifts it back to her husband and then is divorced before consummation (khalwah). The commentator explains that she must return half of what she received, because only half of the dower was actually owed to her at the time of divorce (since the full dower becomes confirmed only after consummation). The key legal principle underlying this ruling is that dirhams and dinars are not specified (لا تتعين) in contracts and rescissions. This means that when the husband gave the wife one thousand dirhams as mahr, that specific sum was not tied to the specific coins; rather, it was a debt obligation. Similarly, when the wife then gifted that sum back to him, the gift did not transfer the specific coins she had received as her property, but rather the fungible value. Therefore, her gift does not bar the husband's right to reclaim the half that was not actually due. The commentator also distinguishes between fungible goods (mithliyyat) like dirhams, dinars, and other measured or weighed items, which are not specified in contracts, and non-fungible goods (qimiyyat), which are specified. An important intra-Hanafi dispute is mentioned in a footnote: if the wife received more than half (e.g., six hundred) and gifted the remainder (four hundred) before divorce, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa ('indahu), she only returns the excess over half (one hundred), while according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) ('indahuma), she returns half of what she actually received (three hundred). The passage also clarifies various scenarios: if she received less than half and gifted it, she owes nothing extra; if she received exactly half and gifted it, she must return half of the full mahr; and if she sold the mahr item to her husband, he recovers half its value.

Key Terms
الدراهم والدنانير لا تتعين في العقود (al-darāhim wa al-danānīr lā tataʻayyan fī al-ʻuqūd): Dirhams and dinars are not specified in contracts; they are considered fungible goods so that their identity is not legally relevant; repayment or return can be in like kind.
الهبة (al-hibah): A gift; transfer of ownership without exchange. Here, the wife's transfer of the mahr amount back to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wife receives a mahr of 1000 dirhams, gifts it back to her husband, and is divorced before consummation. How much must she return according to the Hanafi ruling in the matn?
A) 1000 dirhams
B) 500 dirhams
C) Nothing
D) 250 dirhams

Key Takeaway
When a wife receives full mahr and gifts it back before a pre-consummation divorce, she must return half because the gift does not specify the mahr money due to the fungibility of dirhams and dinars.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
12 min
Gift of Mahr and Its Effect on Divorce Before Consummation
Ruling on wife gifting mahr before or after receipt, then divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on gift of mahr before or after possession and compute the return due upon divorce before consummation, distinguishing the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Gifting the mahr is a debt cancellation; if the wife never took possession, no return is due.

When a wife gifts her mahr to her husband, does she owe anything if divorces occurs before consummation? The answer depends on how much she had taken. This lesson unpacks the nuanced rules from the Hanafi tradition, clarifying that the gift is effectively an ibra' (acquittal) and that an intra-Hanafi dispute arises when she takes more than half.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios
List the three scenarios: wife never took possession, wife took half then gifted all, wife took more than half and gifted the remainder. For each, note the default ruling.
2
Apply the default rule
In the first two scenarios, the wife owes nothing upon divorce because the husband already receives half (or more) due to the gift. Check the condition that she did not take more than half.
If she took less than half and gifted it, no return.
3
Handle the exception
If she took more than half and gifted the rest, she must return the excess over half (Abu Hanifa) or half of what she took (Sahibayn). Work through an example: mahr 1000, she took 600, gifted 400. Calculate each view.
Excess over half = 100 (600 - 500). Half of what she took = 300.
4
Understand the legal nature of the gift
The 'gift' of mahr is actually isqat (cancellation) of the husband's debt. It is valid even without possession because it is ibra' from the creditor. Contrast with a regular gift.
Key distinction: hibah of debt by the debtor is not allowed, but ibra' is.
5
Apply to specific items
If the mahr is a specific item (like an animal), the same rules apply. If she sells it to him, the husband gets half its value back.

كتاب النكاح باب المهر وإن لم تقبضه، أو قبضت نصفه، ثم وهبت الكل، أو ما بقي، أو وهبت عرض المهر قبل قبضه، أو بعده لا.
قوله : وإن لم تقبضه؛ أي ذلك الألف الذي سمي في العقد.

Book of Marriage, Chapter of Dower. And if she did not take possession of it, or she took possession of half of it, then she gifted the whole, or what remained, or she gifted the property of the dower before taking possession or after, [then] nothing [is due]. His saying: 'And if she did not take possession of it' meaning that thousand which was named in the contract. His saying: 'half of it' is a precaution against the case where she took possession of more than half, then gifted all of it and was divorced before consummation: then she returns to him what exceeds half. And if she took possession of less than half and gifted it, then was divorced before consummation, he does not claim anything from her. Thus in 'al-Bahr'. His saying: 'then she gifted the whole' meaning all of the named dower which is the thousand; this applies to two scenarios: the scenario of not taking possession of anything from it, and the scenario of taking possession of half. And the meaning of her gifting the thousand after taking possession of half is that she gifted to him what was taken and other than it. So specifying the gift of the whole to the first scenario only, as done by the author of 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar', has no basis. His saying: 'or what remained' is specific to the second scenario: that is, she took possession of half of her dower and released him from the remainder; and it has no place in the first scenario because 'what remained' implies taking possession of something, and since there is none, it is not. His saying: 'or she gifted' meaning all or more than half; and if she gifted less than half of a specific dower property, she returns what exceeds half; and if she sold it to her husband, he takes back half of its value. (1) The restriction to taking possession of half is to exclude the case where she took more than half and gifted the remainder: then she returns to him what exceeds half according to him (Abu Hanifa), as if she took six hundred and gifted four hundred, then he takes back one hundred; but according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) she returns half of what she took, so she returns three hundred. See 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' (3:171). (2) 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' (3:170). His saying: 'property of the dower before taking possession or after, [then] nothing': meaning he does not take back anything from her. The explanation of the cases: that if she did not take possession of anything, then she gifted the whole: i.e., she remitted it from the husband's liability, then he divorced her before intercourse, then nothing is upon her because the ruling of divorce before consummation is that half the dower is surrendered to him, and that has been obtained, and more, and the woman did not take anything to return to him, unlike the first case, which is that she took possession of a thousand named, then she gifted it to him, and was divorced before intercourse. And if she took possession of half the dower, then she gifted the whole to him, or gifted the remainder, then he divorced her before intercourse, [then nothing is upon her]. Thus in 'al-Bahr'. [1] His saying: 'property of the dower'; the idafah is explanatory, and 'arad' with two fatahs means goods, and what is intended by it is that which becomes specified by specification in contracts and rescissions among specific items; meaning he married her for goods such as an animal, for example, then she gifted it to him before or after taking possession, then he divorced her before consummation, he does not take back anything from her. [2] His saying: 'if she did not take possession of anything' means in the scenario where the dower is of the type that does not become specified by specification. [3] His saying: 'i.e., she remitted it' from 'hatt' which is cancellation; and in it is a rebuttal of what is said: how can she gift what she has not taken possession of and does not own? For gifting what is not in her ownership is not permissible. The gist of the rebuttal: that 'gift' here is intended to mean cancellation from the one on whom it is owed. If you say: they have explicitly stated that gift of a debt is not permissible unless it has been taken possession of? I say: this is regarding gifting to someone other than the debtor; as for gifting the debt by the debtor himself, it is permissible because it is cancellation and acquittal. [4] His saying: 'and that has been obtained' because she has gifted the whole to him, so he has obtained the whole in addition to half. [0] His saying: 'then she gifted the whole' indicates by this that the author's statement 'then she gifted the whole' pertains to both scenarios, and his statement 'or the remainder' pertains only to the second scenario, as we mentioned previously.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the Wiqayah addresses the ruling when a wife gifts her mahr (dower) to her husband before or after taking possession of it, and then divorce occurs before consummation. The passage explains the matn's statement that if she did not take possession or took half then gifted the whole or remainder, or gifted a specific dower property before or after possession, then the husband does not get back anything. The commentator explains each part: 'if she did not take possession' refers to the case where she never took the dower, then gifted it; she owes nothing even if divorce occurs before consummation because the husband already gets half of the dower (by divorce), and she gave him the whole, so he loses nothing. However, if she took more than half and then gifted the whole, she must return the excess over half. If she took less than half and gifted it, she owes nothing. The gift of the entire dower after taking half means she gives the half she took and releases the remaining half from his debt. The text notes that the author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar incorrectly restricted the gift of the whole to the first scenario only. The phrase 'or what remained' applies only when she has taken half and then releases him from the remaining half. If she gifts only part of a specific dower property (like a sheep), she must return any amount over half if divorce occurs. The passage also clarifies a key fiqhi point: if she sells the dower property to her husband, then he can take back half its value. A crucial intra-Hanafi dispute is noted: if she took more than half and gifted the remainder, Imam Abu Hanifa holds she only returns the excess over half (e.g., if she took 600 and gifted 400, she returns 100), while the two students (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold she returns half of what she took (300). The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is not explicitly given here but typically follows Abu Hanifa. The commentary also explains that when the dower is a specific item (like an animal) that becomes specified in the contract, the same ruling applies: if she gifts it, she owes nothing. The passage then addresses an objection: how can she gift something she hasn't taken possession of? The answer: 'gift' here means 'cancellation' (isqat) of the husband's debt, which is valid. Gifting a debt by the debtor (here the wife is the creditor) is permissible as it is considered ibra' (acquittal). Thus, the overall rule: a wife's gift of the mahr to her husband, whether before or after receipt, generally extinguishes his obligation, and upon divorce before consummation, no refund is required except in the specific case where she gave only part of what she took and kept some, then she must return any excess over half.

Key Terms
هبة (hibah): Gift, but here it means cancellation (isqat) of the husband's debt when gifted by the creditor (wife) to the debtor (husband).
قبض (qabd): Taking physical possession of the mahr.
عرض ('arad): Property other than currency, such as goods or animals, that becomes specific (mut'ayyan) by designation in the contract.
إسقاط (isqat): Cancellation or remission of a right or debt.
إبراء (ibra'): Acquittal; releasing the debtor from liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wife receives 500 out of a 1000 dower, then gifts the remaining 500 to her husband. She is then divorced before consummation. How much must she return?
A) 500
B) 0
C) 250
D) 100

Key Takeaway
The wife's gift of the mahr is an ibra' (acquittal); upon divorce before consummation, she generally owes nothing unless she took more than half, in which case an intra-Hanafi dispute arises on the amount to return.

Ruling on Gift of Mahr Before Divorce
Expands the ruling on mahr gift before divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife gifts the mahr to her husband before consummation divorce and distinguish between specific and non-specific mahr in that context.

Core Idea
Gifting the whole specific mahr cancels the husband's right to half; for non-specific mahr, he still gets half.

In Hanafi law, when a divorce occurs before consummation, the husband is entitled to half the mahr. However, this lesson examines a situation where the wife voluntarily gives the entire mahr to the husband through a gift (hibah) or remission (hatt). The ruling depends on whether the mahr is a specific article (like a slave or animal) or a non-specific debt (like cash). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rule to real marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine that the wife has given the whole mahr (or a part) to the husband before the divorce, and that the divorce occurs before consummation.
2
Determine the type of mahr
Is the mahr a specific article (mu'ayyan, e.g., a particular horse) or non-specific (e.g., 1000 dirhams in the husband's liability)? This affects how the gift is treated legally.
Specific articles are determined by identity; non-specific items are determined by value.
3
Apply the rule for full gift
If she gifted the whole mahr, the husband takes nothing. For a specific article, she returned the exact item; for non-specific, she remitted the debt. In both cases, he receives his full entitlement (the whole mahr) and even more, so no further claim.
4
Apply the rule for partial gift
If she gifted less than half, the husband recovers the difference to make up half. If she gifted exactly half, she owes nothing. If she gifted more than half, the husband takes nothing because he already received more than his due.
This applies regardless of whether the mahr is specific or non-specific.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Shafi'i school generally holds that the gift does not cancel the half-right; the husband can still claim half the mahr from the wife even after the gift. The Hanafi position relies on the specific vs non-specific distinction to limit recourse.
This ikhtilaf is not explicit in this passage but is a known point of contention.

The gift of the dower before taking possession or after it, no: meaning she does not return anything to him. The description of the issues: If she did not take anything, then she gifted the whole: i.e., she remitted it from the husband's liability, then he divorced her before intercourse, then nothing is due from her, because the ruling of divorce before consummation is that half of the dower is surrendered to him, and it has occurred with increase, and the woman did not take anything to return to him, unlike the first issue, which is that she took a named thousand, then gifted it to him, and was divorced before intercourse. And if she took half the dower, then gifted the whole to him, or gifted the remainder, then he divorced her before intercourse, as in al-Bahr. [1] His saying: 'the gift of the dower' – the construct is explicative, and al-'arad (with two fathas) is goods, and by it is meant what is determined by specification in contracts and dissolutions among specific articles; meaning he married for goods like an animal for example, then she gifted it to him before possession or after, then he divorced her before consummation, he does not take anything from her. [2] His saying: 'if she did not take anything' – i.e., in the case where the dower is something that is not determined by specification. [3] His saying: 'i.e., she remitted it' – from al-hatt, which is cancellation, and in it is a repudiation of what is said: how can she gift what she has not taken possession of nor owned, for gifting what is not in her ownership is not permissible. The gist of the repudiation: that gifting here is meant as cancellation from the one to whom it is due. If you say: they explicitly stated that the gift of a debt is not permissible unless he takes possession? I say: this is in the gift to someone other than the debtor, but the gift of the debt from the one on whom it is due is permissible because it is a cancellation and acquittal. The half. [4] His saying: 'and it has occurred' – for she gifted the whole, so the safety of the whole accrued to him, rather than half. (1) Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq (3:171). And if the dower was a specific article, and she took possession of it, then gifted it to him, or she did not take possession and remitted it from his liability, then he divorced her before intercourse, then nothing is due from her. As for the case of non-possession, for what has passed. And as for the case of possession, similarly; because she gifted the specific article to him, so the possession of the dower was annulled; because specific articles are determined, unlike the first issue. [1] His saying: 'as we mentioned' – meaning that the ruling of divorce before consummation is that half is surrendered to him, and that has occurred for him in both cases, rather with an increase in the case of the gift of the whole, for then the whole is surrendered to him. [2] His saying: 'and if' – this is an explanation of the third case of cases of non-recourse. [3] His saying: 'then she gifted it' – he pointed to the difference between possession of a specific article and non-possession, where he expressed in the first with the word 'gift' and in the second with 'remission', because as has passed, gifting what is not in one's possession and ownership is meant as cancellation and acquittal. [4] His saying: 'for what has passed' – that the desired result has occurred for him, which is the safety of half with an increase if she gifted the whole specific article or more than half. Yes, if she gifted less than half, the right of recourse is established for him because half safety has not occurred, as has passed. [5] His saying: 'so it was annulled...' – its summary: that specific articles are determined in contracts and dissolutions, so even if he married on a specific slave, for example, he may not keep it and give another, so when he gave it as a dower, then she gifted it to him per se, the previous possession was annulled, and that thing itself returned to him by way of gift, so the safety of half accrued to him, rather with an increase, so he takes nothing from her. [6] His saying: 'unlike the first issue' – which is if she took a named thousand and the like, things that are not determined by specification, then she gifted it to him, then the husband takes back half; because dirhams and others are not determined in contracts, so by her gift the very thing that is his right does not reach him, although the measure of what he gave reaches him; and it is not so here, because the specific article is determined, so by the gift the very thing that is his right reaches him, so the right of recourse does not remain for him.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of a ruling in the Hanafi school regarding the gift of the dower (mahr) by the wife when divorce occurs before consummation. The main ruling states that if the wife gives the entire dower (whether by gift or remission) to the husband, then he divorces her before consummation, she does not owe him anything. This is because the normal rule in Hanafi fiqh is that when divorce occurs before consummation, the husband is entitled to half the dower. If the wife gives him the whole dower, he has received more than his entitlement, so there is no obligation on her to pay anything further. The commentary distinguishes cases based on whether the dower is a specific article (such as a slave or animal) or a non-specific item (such as cash). If it is a specific article, the gift to the husband returns the exact same item to him, effectively annulling the previous transfer and giving him complete ownership. If it is non-specific (like cash), the husband only receives value equal to the dower but not the exact same coins, so he may still claim the half share. The text also explains that if the wife had not yet taken possession of the dower, her remission (hatt) is considered a cancellation of debt, which is valid from the debtor himself. Overall, the passage clarifies that the husband's right to half the dower is satisfied by the wife's generous act of giving the whole dower, and therefore he cannot claim anything extra.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The dower or marriage gift given by the husband to the wife; in this context, it can be a specific article or a non-specific amount.
عرض ('arad): A specific article (e.g., a slave, animal, or distinct item) that becomes determined by specification in the contract.
حط (hatt): Remission or cancellation of a debt; used here when the wife waives the dower due from the husband before taking possession.
هبة (hibah): Gift; in the context of the wife giving the dower to the husband after taking possession.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a wife receives a specific slave as mahr, takes possession, then gifts the slave to her husband, and he divorces her before consummation, what does the husband get?
A) Half the slave's value.
B) Nothing.
C) The entire slave (but must return half).
D) The slave because it was a gift.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes specific from non-specific mahr when the wife gifts it before divorce, ensuring the husband's half-right is either fulfilled by the returned item or adjusted by compensation.

Waiving Specific Dower Before Consummation
Ruling on waiver of specific dower before consummation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a wife returns a specific dower before consummation and explain why it differs from the case of fungible dower.

Core Idea
If the wife returns the exact specific dower, the husband receives his due – she owes nothing more.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced ruling from al-Wiqaya concerning the wife's waiver of a specific dower before consummation. The matn states that in such cases, the wife owes nothing, even if divorce occurs. The commentary explains the legal reasoning, highlighting the crucial distinction between specific commodities ('arad) and fungible items like dirhams. This ruling relies on istihsan, setting aside an analogy drawn by Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The matn covers two cases: (1) wife took possession of the specific dower and then gifted it back to the husband; (2) wife did not take possession and waived the debt. In both, she owes nothing after divorce before consummation.
2
Recognize the key distinction
Specific commodities ('arad) are determined by their essence; they are not fungible like dirhams. In contracts, 'arad must be transferred as a specific item, not replaced with an equivalent.
Contrast with dirhams, which are fungible and not determined by specific identity.
3
Apply the reasoning of istihsan
When the wife returns the exact item, the husband receives his exact right (the specific commodity) back. Whether she returns all (gift) or waives less than half, the husband gets at least half. Hence, she owes nothing. Istihsan overrides qiyas to fungible dower.
The commentary highlights that even if she gifts the whole, the husband gets more than half.
4
Contrast with Zufar's qiyas
Zufar analogized to the case of non-specific dower (dirhams) where the husband can reclaim half. The Hanafi response: dirhams are not specific, so returning an equivalent amount does not give the husband his exact right; but with 'arad, the exact item is returned, so the husband is satisfied.
This practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) means in the specific dower case the wife owes nothing.

Source Text

ولو كان المهر عرضاً فقبضته، ثم وهبته له، أو لم تقبضه فحطته عن ذمته، ثم طلقها قبل الوطء فلا شيء عليها. أما في صورة عدم القبض فلما مر وأما في صورة القبض فكذلك؛ لأنها وهبت العرض له، فانتقض القبض والمهر؛ كان ؛ هذا بيان للصورة الثالثة من صور عدم الرجوع. قوله : ثم وهبته ؛ أشار إلى الفرق بين قبض العَرَض وعدم قبضه حيث عبر في الأول بلفظ : «الهبة»، وفي الثاني بلفظ : «الحطّ» لِمَا مرَّ أن هبة ما ليس في قبضه فإن هناك يرجعُ الزوج بالنصف ؛ لأن الدراهم وغيرها لا تتعين في العقود، فلم يصل إليه بهبتِها عين حقه وإن وصل إليه مقدار ما أعطاه ، ولا كذلك هاهنا، فإنّ العرض متعين فيصل إليه عين حقه بالهبة فلا يبقى له حق الرجوع. وقد قاس زفر هذه المسألة على المسألة الأولى، وما ذكرنا من وجه الفرق استحسان، ومن هنا يعلم وجه الرجوع فيما إذا باعت العرض منه ، فإنه وصل إليه في هذه الصورة بعوض، وهو الثمن والسلامة بعوض كلا سلامة. قوله : فإن الدراهم ... الخ ؛ قال في «البحر» : «قد ظهر لي أن هذه المسألة على ستين وجهاً : أن المهر إما ذهب أو فضة أو مثلي غيرها أو قيمي، فالأول على عشرين وجهاً ؛ لأن الموهوب إمَّا الكل أو النصف، وكلٌّ منهما إما أن يكون قبل القبض أو بعده أو بعد قبض النصف، أو أقل منه أو أكثر، فهذه عشرة، وكل منها إما أن يكون مضروباً أو تبراً، فهي عشرون والعشرة الأولى في المثلي ، وكل منهما إما أن يكون معيناً أو لا، وكذا في القيمي». انتهى
If the dower was a specific commodity and she took possession of it, then gave it to him as a gift, or she did not take possession and waived it from his liability, then he divorces her before consummation, she owes nothing. As for the case of non-possession, it is as previously mentioned. As for the case of possession, likewise; because she gifted the commodity to him, so possession and the dower are invalidated; because commodities are specific, unlike the first issue. [Commentary on the matn]
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the matn of Al-Wiqaya regarding the dower (mahr) when it is a specific commodity ('arad) and the wife either gives it back or waives it before consummation, then the husband divorces her. The ruling states that she owes nothing. The commentary by Imam al-Mahbubi explains the reasoning: in both cases (possession or not), the husband obtains his half or more, so he cannot reclaim. The key distinction is that a specific commodity ('arad) is determined ('ayn) in contracts, unlike dirhams which are not. Thus if the wife gifts the actual item back, the husband receives his exact right. If she waives it without possession, it counts as a waiver of debt. The commentator also mentions that if she gifts less than half, the husband can reclaim the balance. The footnote from Al-Bahr outlines the many permutations of this scenario, categorizing by type of dower (gold, silver, other fungible, or valuable) and amount given back. This ruling relies on istihsan, differing from Zufar's qiyas who analogized it to the earlier case of non-specific dower.

Key Terms
عرض ('arad): A specific, non-fungible commodity (e.g., a slave, a garment) that is determined by its essence.
هبة (hibah): A gift transferring ownership of a specific item from the wife back to the husband.
حط (hatt): Waiver or remission of a debt or obligation, used when the wife has not yet received the dower.
انتقض القبض (intaqada al-qabd): Invalidation of previous legal possession; here, the earlier possession of the dower is undone because the wife returns the exact item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Half the value of the commodity.
B) Nothing.
C) The full value of the commodity.
D) A penalty equal to the dower.

Key Takeaway
When the wife returns the exact specific dower before consummation, the husband receives his due, and she owes nothing further.

Conditional Dower Based on Residence or Travel
Explaining the ruling when dower amount depends on whether husband moves wife or not

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a dower conditioned on the husband's action (e.g., not moving the wife) and determine the applicable dower amount based on fulfillment or breach.

Core Idea
A valid condition in marriage determines the dower amount; fulfillment or breach dictates what is owed.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains a ruling from the matn: when a man marries with a dower that varies based on his actions—such as staying with her or moving her—the dower owed depends on whether he fulfills the condition. The Hanafi school upholds such conditional dower agreements as valid and enforceable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base scenario
Read the text to understand the marriage contract scenario: a man marries a woman with a dower that is conditional on his future actions.
The condition is attached to the dower, not the validity of the marriage.
2
State the condition and the dower options
Note the conditions mentioned: 'on condition that he does not take her out' or 'if he stays, one thousand; if he takes her out, two thousand'.
The condition can be about not moving her or not marrying another.
3
Determine the husband's actual action
Check whether the husband fulfilled the condition (e.g., did not move her) or breached it.
The text uses 'waffā' (he fulfilled) to indicate compliance.
4
Apply the ruling
If he fulfilled, he owes the lesser dower; if he breached, he owes the greater.
The commentary clarifies that the higher dower becomes due upon breach.
5
Recognize the Hanafi position
Understand that the Hanafi school validates such conditions and makes the dower contingent on them.
This differs from schools that may not enforce such varying dower conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن نكح بألف على أن لا يخرجها، أو لا يتزوج عليها، أو بألف إن أقام بها، وبألفين إن أخرجها، فإن وفى، وأقام. قوله : وإن نكح ؛ بمعنى نكح بامرأة بألف مهراً بشرط أن لا يخرجها من تلك البلدة : أي لا يسافر بها أو من بيتها أو بشرط أن لا يتزوج امرأةً أُخرى ما دام هي في نكاحها. قوله : أو بألف ؛ يعني تزوّج ورد، وفي المهر بأنه هو ألف إن أقام بها في البلدة، وألفان إن أخرجها. قوله : فإن وفى ؛ ماض من وَفَّى يَفي أو من التوفيه : أي فإن أتى بما شرط عند العقد : وهو عدم إخراجها، أو عدم التزوج عليها.
If he marries with a thousand on condition that he does not take her out (of town), or does not marry another woman, or with a thousand if he stays with her, and two thousand if he takes her out, then if he fulfills and stays. [Commentary]
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage states a ruling from the matn about conditional dower. If a man marries a woman with a dower of one thousand on the condition that he will not move her from her town or will not marry another woman while she is his wife, then if he fulfills that condition, he owes only the one thousand. Alternatively, if the dower is specified as one thousand if he stays with her, but two thousand if he moves her out, then if he fulfills the condition (i.e., does not move her), he pays the lesser amount. The commentary clarifies the terms: 'yukhrijaha' means to take her out of the town or her house; 'yafī' means he fulfills what he promised at the contract. This ruling establishes that such conditional dower contracts are valid, and the amount owed depends on the fulfillment or breach of the condition.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition attached to the marriage contract regarding the dower amount.
ألف بألف (alf bi-alf): One thousand dirhams or dinars as dower.
وفى (waffā): He fulfilled the condition (e.g., did not move her or did not marry another).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man marries a woman with a dower of 500 if he stays in her town, and 1000 if he moves her. He then moves her. What is the correct dower?
A) 500, because he fulfilled the condition of staying?
B) 1000, because he breached the condition by moving her.
C) The dower becomes the minimum (500) because the condition is void.
D) He owes nothing as the condition is invalid.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a condition attached to the dower that varies the amount based on the husband's action is valid; the dower owed depends on fulfillment or breach of the condition.

Nikah — Marriage

Marriage with Conditional Mahr: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Contingent Dower
Expansion on marriage with conditional mahr, detailing intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on conditional mahr and distinguish valid from invalid conditions according to Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Core Idea
A contingent mahr based on uncertain future actions is invalid (fasid) per Abu Hanifa; the wife receives mahr al-mithl if the condition is unfulfilled.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explores the validity of conditions in marriage contracts that affect the mahr. It presents an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that conditions benefiting the wife are valid, but those introducing uncertainty (gharar) are invalid, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) view both types as valid. Understanding this distinction is essential for determining the correct mahr when contingencies are involved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage discusses two scenarios: (a) marriage for 1000 on condition that the husband does not take the wife out or does not marry another woman; (b) marriage for 1000 if he stays, 2000 if he takes her out. Distinguish the first condition (a benefit to the wife) from the second (a contingent mahr).
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds the first condition valid (sahih) because it benefits the wife and is certain. The second condition is invalid (fasid) because it introduces risk (mukhatara) – the husband does not know if he will take her out. Upon fulfillment, she gets the stipulated mahr; upon breach, mahr al-mithl.
3
State the two companions' position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold both conditions valid as independent alternatives, analogous to marrying on condition of beauty or ugliness where both amounts are known at the time of contract.
4
Analyze the distinguishing reasoning
Abu Hanifa distinguishes the beauty/ugliness case because the wife's quality is observable (mushahadat), reducing ignorance, whereas the husband's future action is uncertain. The two companions see no distinction because both conditions are specified alternatives.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: If the husband stays, both agree she gets 1000. If he takes her out: Abu Hanifa gives mahr al-mithl; the two give 2000. The mufta bihi follows Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
