Wife's Right to Withhold for Mahr: A Hanafi Analysis
States wife's right to withhold and maintenance with qiyas and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a wife's right to withhold herself for unpaid prompt mahr, explain the qiyas analogy to sale, and distinguish the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A wife may lawfully withhold herself for unpaid prompt mahr; her maintenance continues because she is not nashizah.

This lesson expands on a key Hanafi rule: a wife's right to refuse intimacy and travel until she receives her prompt mahr. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah not only states the ruling but grounds it in a powerful qiyas (analogy) to a seller's right of retention. It also highlights a significant intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of prior consent to intercourse. Understanding this ruling clarifies the financial protection Hanafi law affords women in marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wife's entitlements
The passage states she may prevent (man') intercourse and travel, and she still receives maintenance if she prevents.
This applies even after intercourse has occurred.
2
Understand the legal classification
The wife's prevention is lawful (mubah) because she is exercising her right to demand the prompt mahr, which is an immediate obligation.
If she withholds for a different reason, she may be nashizah and lose maintenance.
3
Trace the qiyas to sale
The mahr is analogized to a price (thaman) and the wife's body's usufruct to the sold item (mabi'). The seller's right of retention (habs) is transferred to the wife.
Key phrase: 'al-mahr... 'iwaḑ li-manāfi' al-buḍ‘, fa-ṣāra ka-l-bay‘'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa says the husband cannot have intercourse even if she previously consented; the Sahibayn say he can if she previously consented. The passage restricts the dispute to cases where prior consent occurred.
If no prior consent, all agree it is impermissible.
5
Apply the ruling to maintenance
Since her prevention is lawful, she is not nashizah (disobedient), so maintenance remains obligatory even if she withholds, and even after intercourse.
The guardian of a minor bride also has this right.

[1] And she may prevent him from intercourse and travel with her, and she is entitled to maintenance if she prevents, even after intercourse.
Because the rights revert to the contracting party.
[2] 'And she may prevent him from intercourse and travel with her, and (she is entitled to) maintenance if she prevents': i.e., she is entitled to maintenance on condition of prevention, even after intercourse.
[1] His statement: 'because the rights' i.e., the rights of sale: like delivery of the sold item, receipt of the price, etc., all revert to the direct contracting party, whether that party is a guardian or an agent. If the guardian were a guarantor, it would entail one person being both claimant and claimed.
[2] His statement: 'from intercourse' and likewise from its preliminaries, as in al-Nahr: i.e., the wife may prevent her husband from enjoying her before taking the prompt mahr (whether defined by text or custom), and it is not permissible for him to have intercourse with her against her will if her refusal is due to demanding her mahr in his presence. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is permissible, as in al-Muhit. The difference of opinion should be restricted to when he has already had intercourse with her first with her consent; if he has not yet had intercourse nor has she willingly secluded with him, then it is not permissible by agreement. This is in al-Nahr. The reasoning is that the mahr, especially the prompt portion, is recompense for the usufruct of the marital intimacy, so it is like a sale, and the seller has the right to retain the sold item until he receives the price. It is mentioned in al-Fath and others that the guardian of a minor girl also has the right to prevent the husband until he receives her mahr.
[3] His statement: 'and travel with her'—better expression is 'taking out' as expressed in al-Kanz, to include taking her out of her house after the marriage contract, as the commentators of al-Kanz mentioned.
[4] His statement: 'and maintenance' means if the wife prevents her husband from intercourse and similar acts in order to receive the mahr, her maintenance does not lapse, whether she is in his house or her own house, because her prevention in this case is to exact her right, so she is not considered disobedient (nashizah).
(1) i.e., maintenance is obligatory upon the husband according to Imam (Abu Hanifa) even if she prevents herself for her mahr, because it is prevention to exact her right. See Dhakirat al-'Uqba p.190.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on a matn ruling concerning the wife's right to withhold herself and her entitlement to maintenance. The core ruling is that a wife may prevent her husband from intercourse and traveling with her until she receives her mahr (prompt portion). If she does so, she still retains her right to maintenance because her prevention is a lawful exercise of her right; she is not considered a nashizah (disobedient). This holds even if the husband has already had intercourse with her, i.e., after consummation, she can still withhold herself for any unpaid mahr. The commentary discusses a point of intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: according to Abu Hanifa, it is not permissible for the husband to have intercourse with her if she refuses due to unpaid mahr; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, it is permissible if she previously consented to intercourse. The passage further explains the analogy with sale: the mahr is like the price for the usufruct of the body (buda'), so the wife has a right of retention akin to a seller's right to withhold the sold item. Additionally, the guardian of a minor bride has a similar right to prevent the husband until receipt of the mahr. The term 'safar' (travel) is better rendered as 'ikhraj' (taking out) to include any removal from her home. This passage confirms the relied-upon Hanafi position that the wife's right to withhold is valid and does not negate her right to maintenance.

Key Terms
منع (man'): The wife's act of preventing her husband from intercourse and travel until she receives her mahr
نفقة (nafaqah): The wife's maintenance obligation that continues even when she withholds herself lawfully for mahr
معجل (mu'ajjal): The prompt portion of the mahr due immediately upon marriage

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi law, if a wife prevents her husband from intercourse because her prompt mahr has not been paid, what is the ruling regarding her maintenance?
A) Her maintenance is suspended because she is considered disobedient
B) She is entitled to maintenance because her prevention is a lawful exercise of her right
C) She is entitled to maintenance only if she lives in the husband's house
D) Her maintenance is reduced by half

Key Takeaway
A wife's lawful withholding for prompt mahr does not forfeit her right to maintenance; she is not nashizah.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Wife's Right to Withhold After One Act
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wife's right to withhold and nafaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wife's right to withhold intercourse after one act and apply the ruling to determine maintenance entitlement.

Core Idea
Each act of intercourse is independently contracted; delivering one does not obligate the rest, so wife retains right to refuse subsequent acts until dower paid.

The wife's right to withhold herself from her husband until receipt of her prompt dower is well-established in Hanafi fiqh. However, a subtle intra-madhhab disagreement arises when the husband has already had intercourse with her once with her consent. Does that single act extinguish her right to refuse further acts? This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and its practical consequence for maintenance.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify the exact ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: the wife retains her right to withhold even after one act of intercourse or seclusion. She is not nashiz and her maintenance continues.
This is based on the analogy to sale: delivery of part does not obligate delivery of the whole.
2
Identify the opponent and their view (Sahibayn)
State the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani: after one consensual act or seclusion, the wife's right to withhold ceases; she becomes nashiz if she refuses and loses maintenance.
They consider the contracted subject matter as a single unit delivered by the first act.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Sahibayn's reasoning: once she has handed over the usufruct of the vulva (the contracted benefit), she cannot reclaim it; prevention after delivery is tantamount to reclamation.
They view the marriage contract as a bundle of rights delivered all at once.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine Abu Hanifa's counter-argument: prevention after one act is not reclamation but refusal to deliver remaining acts, each separately contracted. The analogy to sale shows that delivering one item does not force delivery of all.
This is a talil (legal reasoning) based on the nature of the countervalue.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, the wife remains entitled to maintenance; under the Sahibayn, she becomes nashiz and loses maintenance. Later fatwa often follows Abu Hanifa's view.
This affects real-life marital disputes over support.

For Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, every act of intercourse is contracted upon, so delivery of some does not necessitate delivery of the rest. [1] His statement: 'or seclusion'; its ruling is known from intercourse by primary analogy, so its mention is for additional clarification. [2] His statement: 'with her consent'; likewise if he had intercourse with her under duress. (1) (3) His statement: 'she no longer has the right to prevent'; then if she prevents, she becomes rebellious with no maintenance, unless she prevents him from intercourse while she is in his house, as in 'al-Bahr'. [4] His statement: 'so she cannot have'; meaning if she has handed over the benefits of the vulva and did not prevent him from taking them, she no longer has the right to prevent, for prevention after that would be reclaiming what she has given. The response on behalf of Abu Hanifa is that prevention from intercourse after intercourse is not reclaiming, but rather a refusal to deliver the remainder after delivering part, for each instance of enjoyment is contracted upon, so delivery of some of its individuals, i.e., one instance of enjoyment, does not necessitate delivery of the rest. Alternatively, it is said: The contracted subject matter is the totality of enjoyments that accrue to him from her, so delivery of some of its parts, i.e., one instance of enjoyment, does not necessitate delivery of the whole nor the rest. [0] His statement: 'contracted upon'; an objection arises: if it were so, then the dower would not become confirmed with a single act of intercourse, for the dower is a countervalue for the contracted subject matter, and if the contracted subject matter were every act of intercourse, the dower would not be confirmed by one act. The response according to what is in 'al-Hidayah' and its commentaries (2) is: The confirmation by one act is due to ignorance of what lies beyond it, and the unknown does not compete with the known; so the matter is built upon the known, confirmed thing. Then when another act occurs, it competes with the first, so the dower becomes a countervalue for it and the first. Then when another act occurs, it becomes a countervalue for the three, and so on. (1) 'al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' 3:192. (2) See: 'al-Binayah Sharh al-Hidayah' 4:256.
Source pages p. 149

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the wife's right to withhold herself from her husband before receiving her prompt dower, and her maintenance during such withholding. The author begins by stating the rule from the matn: the wife has the right to prevent intercourse and travel, and she is entitled to maintenance even if she prevents, even after one act of intercourse. The commentary explains that this right is analogous to a seller's right to retain the sold item until payment, as the dower is a countervalue for the usufruct of the vulva. A key disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) is then introduced. According to Abu Hanifa, the wife may continue to refuse intercourse even after a single act, because each act is a separate, contracted benefit; delivering one does not obligate delivering all. The two disciples hold that once she has consented to intercourse or valid seclusion, she has delivered the contracted subject matter and cannot later withhold—her prevention becomes rebellious (nashiz), losing her right to maintenance. The text also clarifies that if she prevents for her dower, she is not considered nashiz, and her maintenance remains obligatory. A potential objection is addressed: if each act is separately contracted, why does the dower become fully confirmed by one act? The answer is that the dower is established by the first act because the remaining acts are unknown, and the known prevails over the unknown; subsequently, the dower is apportioned across multiple acts as they occur. The passage emphasizes that the dispute only applies when the first intercourse or seclusion was with her consent; without it, all agree she retains her right.

Key Terms
مهر (mahr): The prompt dower (mahr mu'ajjal) that the wife is entitled to receive immediately from the husband upon marriage.
ناشز (nāshiz): A wife who is rebellious and fails to fulfill her marital duties without lawful excuse; she loses her right to maintenance.
خلوة (khalwah): A valid seclusion between husband and wife that legally confirms the dower and establishes rights as if intercourse occurred, with conditions of privacy and capability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a wife has already had one consensual act of intercourse with her husband but has not yet received her prompt dower, may she still refuse subsequent intercourse?
A) No, because consent to one act delivers the entire benefit.
B) Yes, because each act of intercourse is a separately contracted benefit.
C) No, because seclusion alone confirms the dower.
D) Yes, but she loses her right to maintenance.

Key Takeaway
The wife's right to withhold intercourse for unpaid prompt dower continues even after a single consensual act according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because each act is a separate contracted benefit.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Wife's Right to Prevent After One Act
Intra-Hanafi dispute on one act nullifying right of prevention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on whether one act of intercourse or seclusion with consent removes the wife's right to prevent, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Each act of intercourse is a separate contract unit; surrendering one does not surrender all.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: after a wife willingly engages in intercourse or allows seclusion, can she later refuse? The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that her surrender of the subject of the contract (the benefits of the marriage) extinguishes her right to prevent. Abu Hanifa disagrees, holding that each act of enjoyment is an independent unit of the contract, so partial delivery does not imply full delivery. Understanding this dispute clarifies the legal consequences for the wife's right to maintenance and the concept of nushuz.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling: after one act of intercourse or seclusion with consent, the wife retains her right to prevent subsequent acts. Her surrender of one act does not waive the rest.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold the opposite view: one act removes the right because the entire subject of the contract has been surrendered.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Sahibayn's dalil: she has surrendered the subject of the contract (the benefits of the private part), so reclaiming it would be retraction.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine Abu Hanifa's rebuttal: each act of intercourse is a separate 'subject of the contract' ('ayn ma'qud 'alayh). Surrendering some does not obligate surrendering the rest; prevention is not retraction but refusal to deliver remaining units.
The response also addresses an objection about mahr confirmation: mahr is confirmed by one act due to ignorance of future acts, but as more acts occur, mahr is allocated accordingly.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Sahibayn, after one act the wife cannot refuse without becoming nashiz (losing maintenance). According to Abu Hanifa, she can refuse for valid reasons without being nashiz, unless she prevents without excuse.

And according to Abu Hanifa—God have mercy on him—that every act of intercourse is a subject of the contract, so the surrender of some does not necessitate the surrender of the rest.
[1] His statement: 'or seclusion' – its ruling is known from intercourse by a fortiori reasoning, so mentioning it is for greater explicitness.
[2] His statement: 'with her consent' – likewise if he has intercourse with her under duress.
(3) His statement: 'her right of prevention does not remain' – if she prevents she becomes nashiz, having no maintenance unless she prevents intercourse while she is in his house. So mentioned in al-Bahr.
[4] His statement: 'so it does not remain' – meaning when she has surrendered the benefits of the private part and does not prevent him from taking them, she has no right of prevention, for prevention after that would be a reclaiming of what she had surrendered.
And the answer from the side of Abu Hanifa: prevention from intercourse after intercourse is not a reclaiming but rather a refusal to surrender the remainder after surrendering some, because each instance of enjoyment is a subject of the contract, so surrendering some of its individuals, which is one instance of enjoyment, does not necessitate surrendering the rest. Or it may be said: the subject of the contract is the sum total of enjoyments that he obtains from her, so surrendering some of its parts, which is one instance of enjoyment, does not necessitate surrendering the whole nor the rest.
[5] His statement: 'subject of the contract' – an objection arises: If that were the case, the mahr would not be confirmed by one act of intercourse, for the mahr is the consideration for the subject of the contract, and since the subject of the contract is every act of intercourse, the mahr would not be confirmed by one act. And the answer according to al-Hidayah and its commentaries: confirmation by one act is due to the ignorance of what lies beyond it, and the unknown does not compete with the known; so the matter is based on what is actually known. Then when another act occurs, it competes with the first, and the mahr becomes in consideration of it and the first. Then when another act occurs, it becomes in consideration of the three, and so on.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wife's right to prevent her husband from intercourse after one instance of intercourse or seclusion with her consent. The position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) is that such an act removes her right to prevent entirely, because she has surrendered the subject of the contract (the benefit of the entire marriage). Abu Hanifa disagrees: each individual act of intercourse is a separate subject of the contract, so surrendering one does not mean surrendering all. Therefore, she can still refuse subsequent acts. The commentary clarifies that the ruling for seclusion is derived a fortiori from intercourse, and that even forced intercourse does not affect her right. The text then addresses an objection: if each act is a separate subject, why does one act confirm the entire mahr? The answer is that mahr is confirmed by one act because the future is unknown; the first act confirms the mahr as consideration for the entire contract due to uncertainty. As more acts occur, the mahr is increasingly allocated to them.

Key Terms
خلوة (khalwah): Seclusion of a husband and wife in a place where intercourse is possible without hindrance.
ناشز (nāshiz): A wife who refuses to allow her husband intercourse without legal justification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the legal characterization of each act of intercourse in relation to the marriage contract?
A) Each act is part of one indivisible subject.
B) Each act is a separate subject of the contract.
C) Only the first act matters; subsequent acts are optional.
D) Intercourse is not part of the contract; it is a separate agreement.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, each act of marital enjoyment is a distinct contractual unit; surrendering one does not waive the wife's right to refuse subsequent acts, according to Abu Hanifa.

Wife's Right to Prevent Until Receipt of Immediate Mahr
Ruling on wife's prevention for non-payment of immediate mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a wife's right to prevent intercourse due to non-payment of immediate mahr and apply the rule of custom to determine the amount.

Core Idea
A wife may withhold herself until she receives her immediate mahr, even though the marriage is valid without it.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains a key Hanafi rule: a wife has the right to refuse intercourse until she receives the immediate portion (mu'ajjal) of her mahr. This right exists even though the marriage is valid without immediate payment. The text also clarifies that the mahr takes precedence over the marital benefit, drawing an analogy to sale. When no specific amount is set, the local custom determines the immediate portion, not any fixed fraction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and the Ruling
What act is being discussed? The wife's prevention of intercourse. What is the ruling? She has the right to prevent until she receives the immediate mahr.
2
Determine the Basis of the Right
Why does she have this right? Because delivery of mahr takes precedence over delivery of the marital benefit. This is contrasted with a sale of a specific item, where both are delivered simultaneously.
The commentary cites al-Bada'i' for this distinction.
3
Identify the Scope of the Right
Is it only for the full mahr or also part? It applies to the immediate portion, whether whole or part, as stipulated at marriage.
4
Determine the Amount When Not Specified
If the immediate payment is not specified, what is the criterion? Custom ('urf) of the woman's locality determines the customary amount for her equivalent.
The text explicitly rejects fixed fractions like one-quarter or one-fifth, relying on the maxim: 'what is established by custom is like what is established by Shariah.'
5
Note the Validity of the Marriage
Is immediate payment a condition for marriage validity? No, the marriage is valid without it; the right to prevent is a remedy, not a condition. Immediate payment is recommended (mustahabb).
This distinguishes the Hanafi position from possible misunderstandings.

[٤]
[١] قوله : قبل أخذ ما بين ؛ أي لها المنعُ قبل أخذ المقدار الذي بين تعجيله عند النكاح سواء كان ذلك المقدار كل المهر أو بعضه : أي شرط في النكاح أداءه معجلاً، وفي الفور من غير تأخير، ولو قال : لأخذ ما بين ... الخ ؛ لكان أولى ليفيد أن المنع لأجل قبض المهر.

[۲]قوله : أو قدر : أى إن لم يُبين تعجيل الكلِّ أو تعجيل بعضها، فلها المنع لأخذ ما يعجلُ لها منه عرف فاً، قال في «الفتاوي الصيرفية»: الفتوى على اعتبار عرف بلدها من غير اعتبار الثلث أو النصف. وقال في «الخانية»: يعتبر التعارف ؛ لأن الثابت عرفا كالثابت شرعاً.

[٤] قوله : غير؛ بالنصب حال من قدر ما يعجل أو بالرفع ؛ خبر مبتدأ محذوف : أي العبرة في هذا الباب للعرف ، ولا تقدير فيه بالربع أو الخمس، فإن كان الـعـرفُ تعجيل الثمن مثلاً ، فهو المعتبر.
[01 ] قوله : إن لم يُبين ؛ أي التعجيل كلاً أو بعضاً، وكذا تأجيل الكلّ، فإنّه لو
Before taking what was specified for immediate payment, in whole or in part, or the amount that is customarily paid immediately for a woman like her from a mahr like hers, by custom, not restricted to a quarter or a fifth, if not specified.
(‘Before taking what was specified for immediate payment, in whole or in part’): the particle ‘before’ is connected to his statement: ‘and she has the right to prevent him.’ Then what is coordinated with his statement: ‘what was specified for immediate payment’ is his statement: ‘or the amount that is customarily paid immediately for a woman like her from a mahr like hers, by custom, not restricted to a quarter or a fifth, if not specified.’
[1] His statement: ‘before taking what was specified’ – meaning she has the right to prevent before taking the amount whose immediate payment was stipulated at marriage, whether that amount is the entire mahr or part of it: i.e., it was stipulated in the marriage that it be paid immediately, and promptly without delay. If he had said ‘for taking what...’ etc., it would have been better to indicate that prevention is for the sake of receiving the mahr.
And in it is an indication that delivery of the mahr takes precedence over delivery of the benefits of the private part, whether the mahr is a specific item or a debt, unlike a sale where the price is a specific item: in that case both are delivered together, because simultaneous acceptance and delivery here is impossible, unlike in a sale. So said in al-Bada'i‘.
And that it is not required that the woman herself takes possession, rather the taking by her agent or messenger is sufficient. So if she assigned the mahr to a man against the husband, she may refuse until the assignee takes possession. And from this entire discussion it is known: that immediate payment of the mahr in whole or in part is not a condition in marriage; rather it is recommended.
[2] His statement: ‘or the amount’ – i.e., if he did not specify immediate payment of the whole or part, then she has the right to prevent until she takes what is customarily paid immediately to her from it. It is stated in al-Fatawa al-Sayrafiyyah: the fatwa is based on the custom of her land, without considering a third or a half. And it is stated in al-Khaniyyah: custom is considered, because what is established by custom is like what is established by Shariah.
[3] His statement: ‘for a woman like her’ – i.e., custom is considered, and one looks at how much is customarily paid immediately for a mahr like this for a woman like this.
[4] His statement: ‘not’ – in the accusative as a circumstantial qualifier of ‘the amount that is customarily paid’ or in the nominative as a predicate of an omitted subject: meaning the criterion in this chapter is custom, and there is no fixed limit of a quarter or a fifth. So if the custom is to pay, for example, one-eighth immediately, that is the criterion.
[5] His statement: ‘if not specified’ – i.e., immediate payment in whole or in part, and likewise deferment of the whole, for if he...
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage establishes the ruling that a wife has the right to prevent her husband from intercourse until she receives the immediate portion (mu'ajjal) of her mahr. The immediate portion is either what was specified at the marriage contract (whole or part) or, if not specified, the customary amount for a woman of her status. The commentary emphasizes that the mahr takes precedence over the marital benefits; the wife does not have to surrender herself until she receives the mahr. This differs from a sale of a specific item where delivery is simultaneous. The text also notes that the wife can authorize an agent to receive the mahr, and if she assigns the debt to another, she can still refuse until the assignee receives payment. Furthermore, immediate payment of the mahr is not a condition for the validity of the marriage, but it is recommended (mustahabb). When no amount is specified for immediate payment, the customary practice of the locality is considered, not any fixed fraction like a quarter or a fifth. This is based on the legal maxim that custom has the force of law.

Key Terms
معجل (mu'ajjal): The portion of the mahr that is stipulated to be paid immediately at the time of marriage.
عرف ('urf): Customary practice in a particular locality regarding the amount of immediate mahr payment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If no amount is specified for immediate payment of the mahr, how is the immediate portion determined?
A) It is automatically one-quarter of the total mahr.
B) It is determined by the custom of the woman's locality.
C) The husband may choose any amount.
D) The wife must accept whatever the husband offers.

Key Takeaway
A wife may refuse intercourse until she receives her immediate mahr, and if unspecified, custom determines the amount; the marriage remains valid either way.

Wife's Right to Refuse Consummation Until Prompt Dower Paid
Commentary on wife's right to refuse consummation until receiving prompt dower based on custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wife's right to refuse consummation until receipt of the prompt dower, explain how custom determines the prompt amount, and apply the distinction between explicit stipulation and default custom.

Core Idea
The wife may refuse consummation until the prompt dower is paid; custom, not fractions, sets the amount if not specified.

In marriage, the dower is a fundamental right of the wife. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains a critical legal privilege: the wife is not obliged to submit to her husband until she receives the prompt portion of the dower. The commentary also resolves how to determine that amount when the contract is silent, relying on custom rather than arbitrary fractions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the wife's right and its basis
The wife may prevent her husband from consummation (tamkin) until she receives the prompt dower (mahr mu'ajjal). This right is derived from the principle that delivering the dower takes precedence over delivering the benefits of the vulva, analogous to sale.
This is a wajib right, not a condition of marriage validity.
2
Determine the prompt amount when unspecified
If the contract does not specify which portion is prompt, custom ('urf) of the woman's locale determines the amount. No fixed fractions (quarter, fifth) are used; the criterion is what is customary for a woman like her with a dower like hers.
Authorities like al-Fatawa al-Sayrafiyyah and al-Khaniyyah support this custom-based approach.
3
Contrast explicit stipulation vs. default custom
If the parties explicitly state the division (e.g., whole prompt, whole deferred, or part prompt/part deferred), that stipulation overrides custom. The explicit term is binding.
Recourse to custom only when there is no explicit stipulation.
4
Apply the ruling to travel and visiting
Before receiving the prompt dower, the wife may travel (e.g., for necessity) and visit her relatives without the husband's permission. This reinforces her right of refusal.
Husband cannot restrict her mobility until the dower is paid.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi position differs from the Shafi'i school, which does not permit refusal before dower receipt. In Hanafi, the wife has a stronger financial security right.
This ikhtilaf has practical implications for marital obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(1) أي فما بيناه هو المعجل والمؤجل سواء بينا تعجيل الجميع أو تأجيله، او تعجيل البعض، وإلا أي وإن لم يبينا المتعارف فإن كانا في موضع يعجل فيه البعض ويؤجل الباقي إلى الطلاق أو الموت ينظر كم المعجل لمثل هذه المرأة من مثل هذا المهر في متعارف أولئك القوم. ينظر: «كمال الدراية (ق ٢٣٥).

Book of Marriage, Chapter of Dower. 151. Before taking what was specified to be paid promptly in full or in part, or the amount that is customarily paid promptly for someone like her from a dower like hers, customarily, not estimated by a quarter or a fifth, if not specified. (Before taking what was specified to be paid promptly in full or in part): the phrase 'before' is attached to 'she may prevent him'. Then it is conjoined to 'what was specified to be paid promptly'. (Or the amount that is customarily paid promptly for someone like her from a dower like hers, customarily, not estimated by a quarter or a fifth, if not specified.) [1] His statement: 'before taking what was specified' means she may prevent him before taking the amount specified to be paid promptly at the marriage, whether that amount is the whole dower or part of it: i.e., it was stipulated in the marriage that it be paid promptly, immediately without delay. If he had said 'for taking what was specified', it would be better to indicate that the prevention is due to receiving the dower. It contains an indication that delivering the dower takes precedence over delivering the benefits of the vulva, whether the dower is a specific item or a debt, unlike a sale if the price is a specific item, for both are delivered together; because in this case receipt and delivery together are impossible, unlike a sale. Thus in al-Bada'i'. And that the receipt by the woman herself is not required; rather, receipt by her agent or messenger is sufficient. If she transfers the dower to a man against the husband, she may prevent [consummation] until the transferee receives it. From this entire discussion it is known that marriage does not require prompt payment of the dower in full or in part; rather, it is recommended. [2] His statement: 'or amount' means if he did not specify prompt payment in full or prompt payment of part, she may prevent him to take what is customarily paid promptly for her. In al-Fatawa al-Sayrafiyyah: The fatwa is based on the custom of her city, without considering one-third or one-half. In al-Khaniyyah: Custom is considered because what is established by custom is like what is established by law. [3] His statement: 'for someone like her' means custom is considered and one looks at how much is customarily paid promptly for someone like her from a dower like hers. [4] His statement: 'not' in the accusative as a circumstantial qualifier of 'the amount that is paid promptly' or in the nominative as a predicate of an omitted subject: meaning the criterion in this chapter is custom, and there is no estimation by a quarter or a fifth. If the custom is to pay prompt payment of one-eighth, for example, that is what is considered. [1] His statement: 'if not specified' means prompt payment in full or in part, and likewise delaying the whole. Because if he stipulated delaying the whole, or prompt payment of the whole, or prompt payment of part and delay of part, custom is not considered because the explicit overcomes the implied; recourse to implication is only when the explicit is absent. [1] His statement: 'and the prompt and the deferred...' Al-Birjandi said in his commentary: The prompt and the deferred - if they are specified, then that specification is binding. If part is prompt and part deferred, it must be so. If the whole is made prompt in the contract, the whole is to be paid promptly. If the whole is made deferred, he cannot be asked until the term expires, whether the period is short or long. In al-Khazanah: If the whole is deferred, she has no right to demand it until its term, provided the term is known. Similarly if it is unknown with a slight indeterminacy like harvest and threshing. If the indeterminacy is ambiguous like the blowing of the wind and the rain of the sky, the term is not established and is void. Otherwise, the customary: meaning if they do not specify that the whole is prompt or deferred, or if some is deferred and some prompt, one looks at the named dower and the woman, how much of this named dower is customarily prompt and how much deferred for a woman like her. What is mentioned in Majmu' al-Nawazil: that she is decreed half the dower promptly, that is only based on the custom of the people of Samarkand that they promptly pay half. Thus in al-Dhakhirah. [2] His statement: 'and visiting' in the genitive, conjoined to 'need': i.e., going out to meet her family: i.e., her relatives and loved ones. It is possible that it is in the nominative, conjoined to 'travel': i.e., she may visit her family.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on the chapter of dower from al-Wiqayah. It explains a wife's right to refuse her husband access (tamkin) until she receives the prompt portion (mu'ajjal) of the dower. The author first clarifies the phrase 'before taking what was specified to be paid promptly' — meaning the wife may prevent consummation until she actually receives the amount that was stipulated to be paid at the time of marriage, whether that is the entire dower or a part. The commentary notes that delivering the dower takes precedence over the wife's obligation to submit to her husband, analogizing to sale where delivery of price and goods are simultaneous only if the price is a specific item; here, since the wife's benefit is not a tangible object, she can refuse until the dower is handed over. This principle is cited from al-Bada'i'. The wife does not have to receive the dower personally; receipt by her agent or messenger suffices. If she assigns the dower to a third party (hawalah), she may still refuse until that person receives it. The passage then stresses that prompt payment is not a condition for the validity of marriage (it is only recommended).

When the contract does not specify prompt or deferred amounts, custom ('urf) determines what must be paid promptly. The commentator cites authorities like al-Fatawa al-Sayrafiyyah and al-Khaniyyah ruling that the custom of the woman's locale prevails, without rigid fractions like one-third or one-half. The criterion is 'the amount customarily paid promptly for a woman like her from a dower like hers.' The author explicitly rejects any fixed proportion (quarter or fifth); rather, whatever custom dictates (e.g., one-eighth) is binding.

If the contract explicitly states the division (e.g., whole prompt, whole deferred, or part prompt part deferred), then custom is not invoked — the explicit terms override the implied custom. Al-Birjandi's commentary confirms that explicit stipulations are binding, whether the term is short or long. Even if the term is known by customary approximations like 'harvest time,' it is valid; but if completely ambiguous (e.g., 'when the wind blows'), the term is void and the dower becomes immediately payable.

Finally, the passage addresses the wife's right to travel and visit her family before receiving the prompt dower. The phrasing indicates she may travel (e.g., for necessity) and visit her relatives without the husband's permission as long as the prompt dower remains unpaid. This reinforces the wife's leverage until her financial right is satisfied.

Throughout, the author integrates multiple Hanafi sources (al-Bada'i', al-Fatawa al-Sayrafiyyah, al-Khaniyyah, al-Birjandi, al-Khazanah, al-Dhakhirah) showing the richness of the school's internal discourse.

Key Terms
مهر معجل (mahr mu'ajjal): The portion of the dower that is required to be paid immediately or promptly at the time of marriage, as stipulated or by custom.
مهر مؤجل (mahr mu'ajjal): The portion of the dower that is deferred to a future date, either specified in the contract or determined by custom (e.g., upon divorce or death).
عرف ('urf): Customary practice in a particular locality that determines the prompt amount of the dower when not specified in the contract.
تمكين (tamkin): The wife's act of submitting herself to her husband's sexual access; she may withhold it until the prompt dower is received.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, upon what condition may a wife legally refuse her husband sexual access?
A) She may always refuse for any reason.
B) She may refuse until she receives the prompt portion (mu'ajjal) of the dower.
C) She may refuse only if the entire dower is unpaid, even if deferred.
D) She may never refuse; consummation is obligatory immediately.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants the wife the right to refuse consummation until she receives the prompt dower, which is determined by custom when not specified—a ruling that protects her financial interest.

Ruling on Specifying Prompt and Deferred Mahr and Wife's Right to Travel
Ruling on mahr specification and wife's travel rights

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings on mahr specification to determine the wife's right to travel and the binding nature of contractual terms.

Core Idea
If mahr portions are specified, custom is ignored; if unspecified, custom determines. Wife may travel before receiving prompt mahr.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya addresses two interconnected issues in the marriage contract: the effect of specifying prompt (mu'ajjal) and deferred (mu'ajjal) portions of the mahr, and the wife's right to travel before receiving the prompt part. The ruling clarifies that explicit terms override custom, and that a wife's authority to withhold herself is tied only to the prompt portion. This lesson will walk through the key rulings and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is specifying the mahr portions. The ruling: if specified, binding; if not, custom prevails. Also, the wife's travel: permissible before receiving the prompt mahr.
The specification can be all prompt, all deferred, or part each.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The text references al-Barjandi, al-Khazanah, Majmu' al-Nawazil, al-Dhakhirah, and fatwa collections. The principle that explicit overrides indication is foundational.
No direct Quran or Hadith citation; reliance on juristic consensus and 'urf.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof establish the ruling? The explicit term takes precedence over implication; when absent, recourse to custom ('urf) is justified by the need to avoid uncertainty.
The text states: 'al-sarih yafuq al-dalala' (the explicit overrides the indication).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any other school disagree? The text does not mention intra-madhhab dispute. However, cross-madhhab difference exists regarding the use of mafhum al-mukhalafa, which is addressed in a separate lesson.
The primary ruling is uncontested within Hanafi school.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Which position is relied upon for fatwa? The text cites al-Durr al-Mukhtar and al-Multaqa affirming that the wife's authority to withhold is limited to the prompt portion, and if unspecified, custom governs.
The chosen view is that the specification is binding; otherwise custom applies.

Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr

Not after it, and she does not have the right to prevent; because she has received the whole according to the chosen view. Not after it, and she does not have the right to prevent; because she has received the whole according to the chosen view: i.e., if the prompt and deferred were not specified, she does not have authority to withhold herself because she has taken the entire mahr. This ruling is understood from what preceded, for he said: 'or the amount that is customarily prompt...' up to his saying: 'if not specified'; so restricting the authority to withhold to the amount of the prompt indicates by way of implication that she does not have the right to prevent because she has received more than this prompt amount. There is no disagreement that specification by mention in the transmissions indicates negation of the ruling for what is other than it. [1] His statement: 'by way of'; mafhum al-mukhalafa and mafhum al-qayd: meaning that when it was mentioned that her authority to withhold is established before she takes what was specified as prompt, whether promptness of all or some was specified, and the amount that is customarily prompt when promptness was not specified at the contract, then the ruling on the second possibility is conditioned on taking the customary prompt amount. From this it is understood that this ruling is negated when this condition is absent. So it is established that she does not have the right to prevent if promptness is not specified and she takes the entire mahr. [2] His statement: 'There is no disagreement...' etc.; a rebuttal to what may be objected to his statement 'by way of implication', namely that considering mafhum al-mukhalafa, mafhum al-qayd, mafhum al-shart and mafhum al-wasf is not (accepted) by our scholars, but rather it is a proof according to al-Shafi'i, as the scholars of usul have elaborated in their books, and we have previously seen some of this. The summary of the answer is: The disagreement about considering it is only in divine texts and rulings; as for juristic expressions and transmissions, especially in concise texts, there is no disagreement about considering it; rather it is considered by consensus. [3] His statement: 'Specification by mention'; i.e., specifying a description or condition by mention, making it specific among other descriptions and conditions, and attaching the ruling to it indicates negation of that ruling when that condition or description is absent. [4] His statement: 'indicates...' etc.; thus it was mentioned in the book of Nikah from 'al-Musaffa', and the author of 'al-Nihayah Sharh al-Hidayah' stated it explicitly in the chapter on revocation of gifts, and in the book of Taharah in (1) and in 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' (2:358) and it is the fatwa, and it was chosen in 'al-Multaqa' (p. 53), and 'Ghurar al-Ahkam' (1:346), etc.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and commentary from the Hanafi fiqh work 'Umda al-Ri'aya' on the subject of mahr (dower) in marriage. It addresses the effect of specifying the prompt (mu'ajjal) and deferred (mu'ajjal) portions of the mahr and the wife's rights regarding travel and withholding herself. 

The ruling states that if the parties explicitly specify in the marriage contract whether the entire mahr is prompt, deferred, or part of each, then that specification is binding and custom ('urf) is not considered, because the explicit overrides implication. However, if no specification is made, then the local custom regarding what is prompt and deferred is followed. This applies to the wife's right to travel, go out for necessity, and visit her family before receiving the prompt portion of the mahr. Once she has received the entire mahr (both prompt and deferred), she does not have the right to withhold herself from her husband (i.e., she cannot refuse him due to a claim of unpaid mahr). 

The commentary then delves into an important methodological point: the use of mafhum al-mukhalafa (the concept of opposite implication). Although the Hanafi school generally does not accept mafhum al-mukhalafa as a valid proof in divine texts (Qur'an and Sunnah), the commentator clarifies that in juristic expressions and concise texts (mutun) of fiqh, there is no disagreement; it is accepted by consensus. Thus, the reasoning that restricting the wife's authority to withhold to the amount of the prompt portion implies that she has no such authority when she receives the entire mahr is valid within this context. 

The passage draws on several sources: al-Barjandi's commentary, 'al-Khazanah', 'Majmu' al-Nawazil', 'al-Dhakhirah', 'Kamal al-Dirayah', 'al-Niqayah', and 'al-Musaffa', showing the depth of the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
المعجل (al-mu'ajjal): The portion of the mahr that is due immediately (prompt) at the time of the marriage contract or upon demand, as opposed to deferred (mu'ajjal).
المؤجل (al-mu'ajjal): The portion of the mahr that is deferred to a later time, such as upon divorce or death.
المتعارف (al-muta'arif): The customary practice ('urf) that determines the division of prompt and deferred mahr when not specified in the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She may travel without her husband's permission.

C) She may still withhold herself until she receives all the mahr.
D) She must return the mahr if she wants to travel.

Key Takeaway
The wife's right to travel without permission is tied to the prompt portion of the mahr, not the entire amount; explicit contractual terms override custom.

The Use of Mafhum al-Mukhalafa in Hanafi Fiqh Texts
Methodological discussion on mafhum al-mukhalafa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on mafhum al-mukhalafa and apply it to derive rulings from juristic texts.

Core Idea
Hanafis reject mafhum al-mukhalafa in divine texts but accept it in fiqh expressions by consensus.

This passage also addresses a methodological point: the use of mafhum al-mukhalafa (opposite implication) to derive rulings. Although the Hanafi school generally does not consider mafhum al-mukhalafa as a valid proof in the Quran and Sunnah, the commentator clarifies that in juristic expressions and concise texts, there is no disagreement. This lesson explores the distinction and its practical application to the mahr ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the contested point? The validity of mafhum al-mukhalafa as a proof (hujja) in legal reasoning.
The text specifically addresses mafhum al-mukhalafa, mafhum al-qayd, etc.
2
State the Hanafi position
In divine texts (nusus shar'iyyah) and ahkam, Hanafis do not accept mafhum al-mukhalafa. However, in juristic expressions ('ibarat wa riwayat fiqhiyyah), especially concise texts (mutun), it is accepted without dispute.
This distinction is crucial to avoid conflict with Hanafi usul principles.
3
Identify the opposing view
Imam al-Shafi'i and his school accept mafhum al-mukhalafa as a proof in all texts, including divine texts.
The text refers to the Shafi'i position as a hujja for them.
4
Understand the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is to limit the application to non-divine texts. The commentator gives a rebuttal (daf') to potential objections by arguing that the disagreement is only in divine texts; in fiqh texts, there is consensus (la khilaf fi i'tibarihi).
This is a methodological way to justify using mafhum in this context without violating usul.
5
Apply to the case
In the previous ruling, the text deduced that the wife loses her right to withhold after receiving the full mahr via mafhum al-mukhalafa: the condition of not having received the prompt portion implies the opposite when she has received more. This deduction is considered valid in the Hanafi school for this fiqh text.
The commentator cites multiple sources (al-Musaffa, al-Nihayah) to affirm this practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسفر والخروج للحاجة، وزيارة أهلها بلا إذنه قبل قبضه لفظ «المختصر » هذا : والمعجَّلُ والمُؤَجَّلُ إن بينا فذاك)، وإلا فالمتعارف(٢). (والسفر والخروج للحاجة، وزيارة أهلها بلا إذنه قبل قبضه) : أي ولها السفر.... إلى آخره قبل قبض المعجل
اشترط تأجيل الكـل، أو تعجيل الكـل، أو تعجيل البعض وتأجيل البعض لا يعتبر العرف ؛ لأنّ الصريح يفوقُ الدلالة، وإنّما يضطر إلى الدلالة عند انتفاء الصريح. 11 قوله : والمعجل ... الخ ؛ قال البرجندي في «شرحه»: والمُعَجْلُ والمُؤجَلُ إِن بُيِّنا فذاك المبين لازم، فإن كان البعض معجَّلاً والبعض مؤجلاً يجب كذلك، وإن جُعِلَ الكل معجَّلاً في العقد يعجل الكلّ ، وإن جُعِلَ الكلُّ مؤجّلاً لا يطالب إلى حلول الأجل سواء كانت المدة قصيرة أو طويلة.
وفي «الخزانة»: إذا كانت الكل مؤجّلاً ليس لها حق المطالبة إلى أجله بشرط أن يكون الأجل معلوماً، وكذا إذا كان مجهولاً جهالة متقاربة كالحصاد والدياس، فإن كانت الجهالة مبهمة كهبوب الريح وأمطار السماء، فالأجل لا يثبت ويحبط ، وإلا فالمتعارف : أي إن لم يُبينا أن الكلَّ معجّل أو مؤجل، وإلا أن بعضه مؤجل وبعضه معجل ينظر إلى المسمى وإلى المرأة أن مثل هذه المرأة كم يكون لها من هذا المسمى معجَّلاً وكم يكون مؤجلاً.
وما ذكر في «مجموع النوازل»: أنه يقضى لها بنصف المهر معجلاً، فإنما ذلك بناءً على عرف أهل سمرقند أنهم يُعَجِّلون النصف. كذا في «الذخيرة». [٢] قوله : وزيارة ؛ بالجرّ عطف على الحاجة: أي الخروج لملاقاة أهلها : أي أقاربها وأحبابها، ويحتمل أن يكون بالرفع معطوفاً على السفر : أي ولها زيارة أهلها.
(1) أي فما بيناه هو المعجل والمؤجل سواء بينا تعجيل الجميع أو تأجيله، او تعجيل البعض، وإلا أي وإن لم يبينا المتعارف فإن كانا في موضع يعجل فيه البعض ويؤجل الباقي إلى الطلاق أو الموت ينظر كم المعجل لمثل هذه المرأة من مثل هذا المهر في متعارف أولئك القوم. ينظر: «كمال الدراية (ق ٢٣٥).
(۲) انتهى من النقاية (ص۱۸۰).

If deferment of all, or prompt payment of all, or prompt payment of some and deferment of some is specified, custom is not considered because the explicit overrides the indication, and one has recourse to indication only when the explicit is absent. 11 His statement: 'And the prompt... etc.'; al-Barjandi said in his commentary: 'The prompt and deferred if clarified then that clarification is binding; if some is prompt and some deferred, it must be so; if all is made prompt in the contract, then all is prompt; if all is made deferred, it cannot be demanded until the term expires, whether the period is short or long.' And in 'al-Khazanah': 'If all is deferred, she has no right to demand it before its term, on condition that the term is known. Similarly if it is unknown with a proximate ignorance like harvest and threshing. If the ignorance is vague like blowing of wind and rain from the sky, then the term is not established and is nullified.' Otherwise custom prevails: i.e., if they do not clarify that all is prompt or deferred, or that some is deferred and some prompt, then one looks at the specified amount and at the woman — how much of this specified amount would be prompt for a woman like her, and how much deferred. And what is mentioned in 'Majmu' al-Nawazil': that judgment is given for her with half the mahr prompt; that is based on the custom of the people of Samarkand that they prompt half. Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr
153
Not after it, and she does not have the right to prevent; because she has received the whole according to the chosen view. Not after it, and she does not have the right to prevent; because she has received the whole according to the chosen view: i.e., if the prompt and deferred were not specified, she does not have authority to withhold herself because she has taken the entire mahr. This ruling is understood from what preceded, for he said: 'or the amount that is customarily prompt...' up to his saying: 'if not specified'; so restricting the authority to withhold to the amount of the prompt indicates by way of implication that she does not have the right to prevent because she has received more than this prompt amount. There is no disagreement that specification by mention in the transmissions indicates negation of the ruling for what is other than it. [1] His statement: 'by way of'; mafhum al-mukhalafa and mafhum al-qayd: meaning that when it was mentioned that her authority to withhold is established before she takes what was specified as prompt, whether promptness of all or some was specified, and the amount that is customarily prompt when promptness was not specified at the contract, then the ruling on the second possibility is conditioned on taking the customary prompt amount. From this it is understood that this ruling is negated when this condition is absent. So it is established that she does not have the right to prevent if promptness is not specified and she takes the entire mahr. [2] His statement: 'There is no disagreement...' etc.; a rebuttal to what may be objected to his statement 'by way of implication', namely that considering mafhum al-mukhalafa, mafhum al-qayd, mafhum al-shart and mafhum al-wasf is not (accepted) by our scholars, but rather it is a proof according to al-Shafi'i, as the scholars of usul have elaborated in their books, and we have previously seen some of this. The summary of the answer is: The disagreement about considering it is only in divine texts and rulings; as for juristic expressions and transmissions, especially in concise texts, there is no disagreement about considering it; rather it is considered by consensus. [3] His statement: 'Specification by mention'; i.e., specifying a description or condition by mention, making it specific among other descriptions and conditions, and attaching the ruling to it indicates negation of that ruling when that condition or description is absent. [4] His statement: 'indicates...' etc.; thus it was mentioned in the book of Nikah from 'al-Musaffa', and the author of 'al-Nihayah Sharh al-Hidayah' stated it explicitly in the chapter on revocation of gifts, and in the book of Taharah in (1) and in 'al-Durr al-Mukhtar' (2:358) and it is the fatwa, and it was chosen in 'al-Multaqa' (p. 53), and 'Ghurar al-Ahkam' (1:346), etc.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage is a ruling and commentary from the Hanafi fiqh work 'Umda al-Ri'aya' on the subject of mahr (dower) in marriage. It addresses the effect of specifying the prompt (mu'ajjal) and deferred (mu'ajjal) portions of the mahr and the wife's rights regarding travel and withholding herself. 

The ruling states that if the parties explicitly specify in the marriage contract whether the entire mahr is prompt, deferred, or part of each, then that specification is binding and custom ('urf) is not considered, because the explicit overrides implication. However, if no specification is made, then the local custom regarding what is prompt and deferred is followed. This applies to the wife's right to travel, go out for necessity, and visit her family before receiving the prompt portion of the mahr. Once she has received the entire mahr (both prompt and deferred), she does not have the right to withhold herself from her husband (i.e., she cannot refuse him due to a claim of unpaid mahr). 

The commentary then delves into an important methodological point: the use of mafhum al-mukhalafa (the concept of opposite implication). Although the Hanafi school generally does not accept mafhum al-mukhalafa as a valid proof in divine texts (Qur'an and Sunnah), the commentator clarifies that in juristic expressions and concise texts (mutun) of fiqh, there is no disagreement; it is accepted by consensus. Thus, the reasoning that restricting the wife's authority to withhold to the amount of the prompt portion implies that she has no such authority when she receives the entire mahr is valid within this context. 

The passage draws on several sources: al-Barjandi's commentary, 'al-Khazanah', 'Majmu' al-Nawazil', 'al-Dhakhirah', 'Kamal al-Dirayah', 'al-Niqayah', and 'al-Musaffa', showing the depth of the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhum al-mukhalafa): A method of interpretation where a ruling attached to a specific condition or description implies the opposite ruling when that condition or description is absent.
التخصيص بالذكر (al-takhsis bi al-dhikr): Specifying a description or condition by mention, making it specific among others, so that the ruling attached to it indicates its opposite when absent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, where does the Hanafi school accept the validity of mafhum al-mukhalafa?
A) In all texts, including divine and juristic.
B) Only in divine texts.
C) Only in juristic expressions and concise fiqh texts.
D) Nowhere; it is always rejected.

Key Takeaway
Mafhum al-mukhalafa is valid in Hanafi fiqh texts by consensus, though not in divine texts.

Nikah — Marriage

Wife's Right to Refuse After Full Mahr: The Hanafi Intra-School Dispute
Explains the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on wife's withholding right after full mahr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why later Hanafi scholars overruled the original qiyas-based position on the wife's right to refuse after full mahr and identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling.

Core Idea
Custom overrides analogy: the wife loses her right to refuse after receiving the customary prompt mahr, even if the full mahr was paid.

This passage from 'Umda al-Ri'aya delves into an important intra-Hanafi dispute: does a wife have the right to refuse intimacy after receiving the entire mahr when the prompt and deferred portions were not specified? The answer reveals a fascinating interaction between qiyas (analogy) and urf (custom), and shows how later Hanafi scholars refined the school's position to align with prevailing practice. Let's trace the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the original Hanafi position
According to the Zahir al-Riwayah, the wife has the right to refuse intimacy until she receives all the mahr (both prompt and deferred), because the mahr is the exchange for the vulva, analogous to a sale where the seller may withhold goods until full payment.
This is based on qiyas jali (clear analogy).
2
Identify the later scholars' position
The later Hanafi scholars (al-muta'akhkhirun) held that she does not have the right to refuse after receiving the customary prompt amount, even if the entire mahr was paid without specification. They argued that custom (urf) overrides the analogy.
This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position.
3
Analyze the original proof (qiyas)
The original position's proof: the mahr is 'iwad (exchange) for the vulva, just as the price is for a sold item. Therefore, the wife has a right of retention (haqq al-habs) until full payment, just as a seller does.
The qiyas is valid in principle; the dispute is about its application.
4
Analyze the later scholars' proof (istihsan bi al-urf)
The later scholars argued that custom (urf) shows that wives do not withhold themselves after receiving the customary prompt amount. This custom is widespread and consistent, so it overrides the qiyas via istihsan.
Hanafi usul allows custom to override qiyas when it is prevalent.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The later position is the mufta bihi. Practically, a wife who receives the full mahr (without specification) cannot refuse intimacy, whereas under the earlier view she could.
This is the rule applied in later fatwa collections.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا بعده، ولا لها المنع ؛ لقبض الكل في المختار ) : أي إن لم يبين المعجل والمؤجل لا يكون لها ولاية منع النفس ؛ لأخذ كل المهر، فهذا الحكم قد فهم مما تقدم، فإنه ... قال : أو قدر ما يعجل... إلى قوله : إن لم يبين ؛ فتقييد ولاية المنع بقدر المعجل يدل بطريق المفهوم على أن ليس لها المنع ؛ لقبض الزائد على هذا المعجل، ولا خلاف في أن التخصيص بالذكر في الروايات يدل على نفي الحكم عما عداه. قوله : بطريق ؛ مفهوم المخالفة ومفهوم القيد : يعني أنه لما ذكر أن ولاية منعها ثابتة قبل أخذ ما بين تعجيله على تقدير بيان التعجيل كلاً أو بعضاً، وقدر ما يعجل عرفاً على تقدير عدم بيان التعجيل عند العقد، فقيد الحكم على التقدير الثاني بأخذ القدر المعجل علم منه انتفاء هذا الحكم عند انتفاء هذا القيد، فثبت منه أنه ليس لها المنع على تقدير عدم بيان المعجل لأخذ كل المهر. قوله : ولا خلاف ... الخ ؛ دفع لما يرد على قوله بطريق المفهوم، وهو أن اعتبار مفهوم المخالفة ومفهوم القيد ومفهوم الشرط ومفهوم الوصف ليس عند أصحابنا، وإنما هو حجة عند الشافعي كما بسطه الأصوليون في كتبهم. وحاصل الجواب : إن الخلاف في اعتباره إنما هو في النصوص الشرعية والأحكام، وأما في العبارات والروايات الفقهية لا سيما في المتون المختصرة فلا خلاف في اعتباره، بل هو معتبر بالاتفاق. قوله : إن التخصيص بالذكر ؛ أي تخصيص وصف أو قيد بالذكر، وجعله مخصصاً فيما بين غيره من الأوصاف والقيود، وتعليق الحكم به يدل على انتفاء ذلك الحكم عند انتفاء ذلك القيد والوصف. قوله : يدل ... الخ ؛ هكذا ذكره في كتاب النكاح من المصفى، وبه صرح صاحب النهاية شرح الهداية في باب الرجوع في الهبة. ولا لو أجل كله، لكن أراد التصريح بهذا ليدل على أنه مختلف فيه، والمختار هذا، فإن المتأخرين اختاروا هذا بناء على المتعارف ، وإن كان أصل المذهب أن لها ولاية المنع لأخذ كل المهر إذا لم يبين مقدار مهر المعجل والمؤجل ؛ لأن المهر عوض البضع، فما لم تقبض كل العوض لا يجب عليها تسليم البضع. قوله : ولكن ... الخ ؛ حاصله إن الحكم المذكور وإن كان مفهوماً مما سبق لكنه لما كان مختلفاً فيه بين المشايخ أراد التصريح بذكره والتنصيص بالمفتى به. قوله : يدل ؛ يعني التصريح المختار هذا، وهذه الفائدة لا تحصل مما مر إنما يعلم منه مجرد الحكم. قوله : فإن ؛ دفع لما يرد أنه كيف يقول المصنف : إنه المختار مع كونه خلاف ظاهر الرواية. قوله : بناء ؛ يعني أن المتأخرين إنما أفتوا به بناءً على المتعارف، فإن العرف على أنها لا تمنع بعد أخذ المقدار المعجل عرفاً. قوله : لأن ؛ علة لأصل المذهب، وحاصله : إن المهر عوض لمنافع البضع فما لم تأخذ كل المهر يكون لها حق الامتناع من تسليم منافعه : كالبائع له حق حبس المبيع ما بقي درهم من الثمن. فإن قلت : هذه العلة تقتضي أن تكون لها ولاية المنع لأخذ كل المهر في جميع الصور؟ قلت : هَب لكن في صورة بيان التعجيل لكل المهر أو بعضه قد رضيت بإسقاط حقها بعد أخذ المعجل، ولا كذلك في صورة عدم البيان.
Not after it, and she has no right to refuse; because of receiving the whole in the chosen view. That is, if he did not specify the prompt and deferred portions, she has no authority to refuse herself because she took all the mahr. This ruling is understood from what preceded: he said 'or an amount that is prompt...' up to his words 'if he did not specify'; so restricting the authority of refusal to the amount of the prompt indicates by way of implication that she has no right to refuse because of receiving more than this prompt amount. And there is no disagreement that specification by mention in the narrations indicates the negation of the ruling regarding what is other than it. His words 'by way': concept of opposition and concept of the qualifier: meaning that when it was mentioned that her authority to refuse is established before taking what is specified as prompt, on the condition of specifying promptness in whole or in part, and the customary prompt amount on the condition of not specifying promptness at the contract, then the ruling was restricted on the second condition to taking the customary prompt amount, so from that it is known that this ruling is negated when this condition is absent, thus it is established that she has no right to refuse on the condition of not specifying the prompt amount because she received all the mahr. His words 'and no disagreement...': a rebuttal of what might be objected to his statement 'by way of concept', namely that considering the concept of opposition, concept of the qualifier, concept of condition, and concept of description is not according to our scholars; rather it is a proof according to al-Shafi'i. The summary of the answer: the disagreement about considering it is only regarding scriptural texts and rulings; but regarding expressions and jurisprudential narrations, especially in concise texts, there is no disagreement about considering it; rather it is considered by consensus. His words 'that specification by mention': i.e., specifying a description or condition by mention, and making it specific among other descriptions and conditions, and attaching the ruling to it indicates the negation of that ruling when that condition or description is absent. His words 'indicates...': thus he mentioned in the Book of Marriage from al-Mustafa, and the author of al-Nihaya Sharh al-Hidaya in the chapter on returning gifts stated it explicitly. And not even if all is deferred, but he intended to explicitly state this to indicate that it is disputed, and this is the chosen view. Indeed, the later scholars chose this based on custom, although the original position of the school is that she has the authority to refuse until she takes all the mahr if he did not specify the amount of the prompt and deferred mahr, because the mahr is the exchange for the vulva; as long as she has not received all the countervalue, she is not obligated to deliver the vulva. His words 'but...': the summary is that the mentioned ruling, even though it is understood from what preceded, when it was disputed among the shaykhs, he wanted to explicitly mention it and specify the fatwa by it. His words 'indicates': meaning that the explicit statement of this chosen view is a benefit that is not obtained from what preceded; only the bare ruling is known from it. His words 'for': a rebuttal of the objection: how can the author say that it is the chosen view while it contradicts the apparent transmission? His words 'based on': meaning that the later scholars only gave fatwa based on custom; for custom holds that she does not refuse after taking the customary prompt amount. His words 'because': the cause for the original position of the school; its summary: the mahr is the exchange for the benefits of the vulva; so as long as she has not taken all the mahr, she has the right to refuse delivery of its benefits, like the seller has the right to withhold the sold item as long as a dirham of the price remains. If you say: this cause requires that she has the authority to refuse until all the mahr is taken in all cases? I say: granted, but in the case of specifying promptness for all or part of the mahr, she has consented to drop her right after taking the prompt amount, unlike the case of not specifying.
Source pages p. 153

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the wife's right to refuse intimacy after receiving the full mahr when the prompt and deferred portions were not specified at the time of marriage. The author (commentator) explains that the relied-upon position (المختار) among later Hanafi scholars is that she does not have the right to refuse. This contradicts the earlier position (أصل المذهب) which states she retains the right to refuse until all mahr is paid, based on an analogy (qiyas) with a seller's right to withhold goods until full payment. The later scholars (متأخرون) overruled this analogy based on custom (عرف): in their societies, once a wife receives the customary prompt amount, she is not expected to refuse intimacy, even if the deferred portion remains unpaid. The commentator also addresses a methodological point about the concept of opposite implication (مفهوم المخالفة). He clarifies that while some Hanafi usul scholars reject this concept in scriptural interpretation, it is accepted in fiqh texts and commentaries by consensus, especially in concise matns. The ruling is thus a case of istihsan (juristic preference) overriding qiyas due to custom.

Key Terms
مفهوم المخالفة (mafhūm al-mukhālafa): The implication that a ruling is negated when a described condition or qualifier is absent; opposite implication.
المختار (al-mukhtār): The chosen or relied-upon position among later Hanafi scholars, as opposed to the original position of the school.
المتعارف (al-muta‘āraf): Prevailing custom or common practice, used here as the basis for the later Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in this passage, when does the wife lose her right to refuse intimacy?
A) Only after receiving the entirety of both prompt and deferred mahr
B) After receiving the customary prompt amount, even if the entire mahr was paid without specification
C) She never loses the right to refuse until all mahr is explicitly specified
D) Only if the mahr is specified as prompt and deferred, and she receives the prompt portion

Key Takeaway
Later Hanafi scholars overrode the original qiyas-based right of refusal with custom (urf), making the wife's right to refuse depend on whether she has received the customary prompt amount rather than the entire mahr.

Wife's Right to Withhold Herself When Whole Mahr is Deferred
Commentary on deferred mahr and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the original Hanafi position on the wife's right to withhold when the entire mahr is deferred, explain the later scholars' custom-based objection, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
The wife's right to withhold for the entire mahr can be overridden by custom if only a portion is normally advanced.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the wife's right to withhold herself (wilayat al-man') when the husband defers the entire mahr without specifying an advanced portion. The original madhhab (zahir al-riwaya) grants her this right, but later scholars (muta'akhkhirun) preferred a view based on custom ('urf). Understanding this dispute clarifies how custom can modify default rulings within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Original Hanafi Position
Identify the ruling from the original madhhab (zahir al-riwaya) concerning the wife's right when the entire mahr is deferred.
The original position is that she has the right to withhold until she receives the full mahr.
2
Identify the Opposing View and Its Basis
Identify the later scholars' view and their reason for adopting a different ruling.
The later scholars based their view on custom ('urf): people normally intend to advance only a portion.
3
Examine the Original Proof (Dalil)
Understand the original proof: mahr is the exchange for intimacy, so the wife is not obliged to surrender intimacy until she receives the full exchange.
This is an analogy (qiyas) to a seller's right to withhold goods until full payment.
4
Analyze the Tarjih (Preference)
Determine why the later view became the mufta bihi (operative ruling) despite the original position.
The text states that the later scholars chose this view, and it is the preferred one for fatwa.
5
Apply the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
Identify the practical difference between the two views in a real-life scenario.
Under the original view, she can refuse travel or intimacy until full mahr; under the later view, she cannot after receiving the customary advanced portion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا لو أجل كله لكن أراد التصريح بهذا ليدل على أنه مختلف فيه، والمختار هذا، فإن المتأخرين اختاروا هذا بناء على المتعارف، وإن كان أصل المذهب أن لها ولاية المنع لأخذ كل المهر إذا لم يبين مقدار مهر المعجل والمؤجل لأن المهر عوض البضع، فما لم تقبض كل العوض لا يجب عليها تسليم البضع. ولا لو أجل كله فإنه لو أجل الكل
And not if the whole [mahr] is deferred. But he intended to explicitly mention this to indicate that it is disputed, and the chosen view is this. Indeed, the later scholars chose this based on custom, although the original madhhab is that she has the right of prevention for taking the entire mahr if he did not specify the amount of the advanced and deferred portions, because the mahr is the exchange for the right to intimacy, so as long as she has not received the entire exchange, she is not obligated to surrender the right to intimacy. And not if the whole is deferred: for if the whole is deferred...
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This is a critical refinement (hashiya) on the sharh of Al-Wiqayah. The passage discusses the ruling concerning when the entire mahr is deferred without specifying the advanced portion. According to the original Hanafi madhhab (zahir al-riwaya), the wife has the right to withhold herself (wilayat al-man') from the husband until she receives the entire mahr, because the mahr is the exchange (iwad) for the right to intimacy (buda'). This is analogous to a seller's right to withhold the sold item until full payment. However, later Hanafi scholars preferred a different view based on the prevailing custom ('urf). They held that after receiving the customary advanced portion (mu'ajjal), the wife no longer has the right to withhold herself, because customarily people only intend to give a portion upfront. The author of the hashya explains that the explicit mention of this ruling in the text is to indicate that it is a matter of ikhtilaf (dispute) among the scholars, and the chosen (mukhtar) view for fatwa is the later one based on custom.

Key Terms
ولاية المنع (wilayat al-man'): The wife's legal right to withhold herself from her husband until she receives her dower.
المهر المعجل والمؤجل (al-mahr al-mu'ajjal wa al-mu'ajjal): The dower that is paid immediately (advanced) and the portion deferred to a later time.
عوض البضع (iwad al-buda'): The exchange for the right to sexual intimacy; the dower is considered compensation for access to that right.
المتعارف (al-muta'arif): The prevailing custom ('urf) that influences legal rulings, especially in matters of dower.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) After receiving any payment, regardless of custom.
B) After receiving the entire mahr.
C) After receiving the customary advanced portion.
D) Never; she can always withhold until full payment.

Key Takeaway
The wife's right to withhold for the entire mahr can be overridden by local custom regarding what is considered the advanced portion.
