Husband's Right to Travel with Wife: Dispute Between Zahir al-Riwaya and Fasad al-Zaman
Critical refinement of a marital travel ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on a husband's right to travel with his wife after paying advanced mahr, and identify how the concepts of fasad al-zaman and maslaha influence the fatwa.

Core Idea
Zahir al-riwaya allows travel; later scholars restrict for fasad al-zaman—the mufti decides based on harm.

This passage refines a seemingly straightforward ruling: the husband's right to travel with his wife after paying the advanced mahr. While the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) grants this right, later Hanafi masters introduced a critical refinement based on the corruption of the times (fasad al-zaman). You will learn why some scholars restrict this right and how the mufti's judgment of harm (mudarrah) and public interest (maslaha) determines the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent ruling
State the ruling of zahir al-riwaya from the passage: the husband may travel with his wife after paying the advanced portion of the mahr.
This is the default position from the core transmissions of the school.
2
Locate the dissenting view
Identify the later scholars (Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar, Abu al-Layth) and the works (Al-Mukhtar, Al-Muhit, Al-Kafi) that restrict this right.
Their key rationale: fasad al-zaman (corruption of the times) makes travel harmful.
3
Analyze the opposing proofs
Examine the arguments: the later scholars rely on the principle of preventing harm (la darar) and the Quranic command 'wa la tudarruhunna' (do not harm them). Al-Qadi counters with the lodging verse (Askinuhunna), arguing the husband's right is primary.
The dispute hinges on whether harm is presumed or must be proven.
4
Assess the tarjih spectrum
Note how various Hanafi works treat the issue: some (Al-Mukhtar, Al-Muhit) choose the restriction; others (Al-Fusul) prefer the original view but allow the mufti discretion based on harm.
Authority_weight shifts from zahir al-riwaya to fatawa mutakhkhirin.
5
Determine the mufti's role
Understand that the final ruling is delegated to the mufti, who must consider the presence or absence of harm (mudarrah) and act according to maslaha (public interest).
This reflects the dynamic nature of Hanafi fatwa, adapting to time and place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وله السفر بها بعد أدائه في ظاهر الرواية أي بعد أداء ما بين تعجيله فقد سقط حقها، فلا يكون لها منع النفس لأخذه. قوله: فقد سقط حقها؛ أي حق منع الزوج؛ لأنه لما رضيت بتأجيل الكل، ومن المعلوم أن النكاح يكون بغرض الاستمتاع في أي وقت شاء، فقد رضيت بإسقاط حقها. قوله: وله؛ أي للزوج أن يسافر بها بعد أداء القدر المعجل شرطاً أو عرفاً، وليس لها الامتناع من ذلك، وكذا له ذلك إذا أدى كل المهر معجلاً كان أو مؤجلاً. قوله: في ظاهر الرواية؛ ذكر في «البحر»: أولاً إنه إذا أوفاها المعجل، فالفتوى على أنه يسافر بها، كما في «جامع الفصولين». ثم ذكر عن الفقيه أبي القاسم الصفار وأبي الليث: إنه ليس له السفر مطلقاً بلا رضاها؛ لفساد الزمان؛ لأنها لا تأمن على نفسها في منزلها، فكيف إذا خرجت؟ وصرح في «المختار» أن عليه الفتوى، وذكر في «المحيط»: إنه المختار، واختاره كثير من مشايخنا، كما في «الكافي». وفوض الأمر فيه إلى المفتي في «البزازية» حيث قال: بعد إيفاء المهر إذا أراد أن يخرجها من بلدها إلى بلاد الغربة يمنع من ذلك؛ لأن الغريب يؤذى ويتضرر لفساد الزمان. كذا اختاره الفقيه وبه يفتي. وقال القاضي: قول الله: أسكنوهن من حيث سكنتم أولى من قول الفقيه، قيل: قوله: ولا تضاروهن... في آخره دليل قول الفقيه؛ لأنه قد علمنا من عادة زماننا مضارة قطيعة في الاغتراب بها. واختار في «الفصول» قول القاضي، فيفي بما يقع عنده من المضارة وعدمها؛ لأن المفتي إنما يفتي بحسب ما يقع عنده من المصلحة.
And he may travel with her after paying it in the apparent narration: i.e., after paying what was specified as his advanced portion. Her right has fallen, so she does not have the right to prevent herself from him for taking it. His statement: 'Her right has fallen' i.e., her right to prevent the husband; because when she agreed to defer the whole, and it is known that marriage is for the purpose of enjoyment at any time he wishes, she has agreed to drop her right. His statement: 'And he may' i.e., the husband may travel with her after paying the advanced portion as a condition or custom, and she cannot refuse that. Similarly, he may do so if he pays the entire mahr, whether advanced or deferred. His statement: 'In the apparent narration'; it is mentioned in 'Al-Bahr': first, if he pays her the advanced portion, the fatwa is that he may travel with her, as in 'Jami' al-Fusulayn'. Then he mentioned from Al-Faqih Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar and Abu al-Layth: that he may not travel absolutely without her consent due to the corruption of the times; because she does not feel safe in her own home, so how when she goes out? And it was stated clearly in 'Al-Mukhtar' that the fatwa is upon it, and it is mentioned in 'Al-Muhit' that it is the chosen view, and many of our shaykhs chose it, as in 'Al-Kafi'. And the matter was delegated to the mufti in 'Al-Bazzaziyya' where he said: after paying the mahr, if he wants to take her out of her town to foreign lands, he is prevented from that because the stranger is harmed and troubled due to the corruption of the times. Thus the faqih chose it and by it he gives fatwa. And Al-Qadi said: The saying of Allah: 'Lodge them where you dwell' is more appropriate than the saying of the faqih. It was said: His saying: 'And do not harm them' at its end is evidence of the faqih's saying; because we know from the custom of our time that harm is definite in taking her abroad. And he chose in 'Al-Fusul' the saying of Al-Qadi, so he decides according to what occurs to him of harm or its absence; because the mufti only gives fatwa according to what occurs to him of maslaha.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This is a critical refinement on the sharh. The passage discusses the husband's right to travel with his wife after paying the advanced mahr. According to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (and according to one view of Abu Yusuf?), the husband may travel with her after paying the mu'ajjal. However, later scholars like Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar and Abu al-Layth argued that he may not travel without her consent due to fasad al-zaman (corruption of the times). They held that since she is not safe even at home, traveling would expose her to greater harm. This view was chosen by many and is the basis for fatwa in some works. The text then presents the view of Al-Qadi who prefers the Quranic verse on lodging (Surah Talaq) and argues that the husband's right to travel is established. The author of Al-Fusul adopts the Qadi's view, but adds that the mufti should judge based on whether harm (madarra) exists in his time. The passage concludes that the mufti must consider maslaha (public interest). This dispute is intra-Hanafi, with the later view restricting the apparent narration due to changed circumstances.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwaya): The apparent or well-known transmission from the founding imams, which is the basis of fatwa unless overridden.
فساد الزمان (fasad al-zaman): The corruption or moral decay of the times, which may justify altering a ruling from zahir al-riwaya to prevent harm.
مضارة (mudarrah): Harm or injury, specifically the harm that may befall the wife if forced to travel despite unsafe conditions.
المصلحة (al-maslaha): Public interest or welfare, which the mufti should consider when determining the ruling in a given time and place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya), what is the ruling on a husband traveling with his wife after paying the advanced mahr?
A) He may not travel without her consent.
B) He may travel with her.
C) He must pay the entire mahr first.
D) He must obtain permission from her guardian.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the ruling on a husband's right to travel with his wife after paying mahr is not absolute; it is refined by later scholars to prevent harm, and the mufti must consider the circumstances of the time.

Husband's Travel with Wife After Mahr: Zahir al-Riwayah and Fasad al-Zaman
Ruling on husband traveling with wife after mahr payment with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on husband traveling with wife after mahr payment and explain why later scholars differed due to fasad al-zaman.

Core Idea
Zahir al-riwayah permits travel, but fasad al-zaman shifts the fatwa to restriction.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school on a husband's right to travel with his wife after paying the mahr. While the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah) grants him this right, later scholars challenged it based on changing times. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi fiqh dynamically responds to social conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
The matn states that according to zahir al-riwayah, the husband may travel with his wife after paying the mahr (expedited portion or full amount). The wife cannot refuse.
This is the ruling from the foundational texts (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).
2
Identify the later objection
Scholars like Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar and Abu al-Layth argue that the husband cannot travel without the wife's consent due to fasad al-zaman (corruption of the times). They cite that if she is not safe at home, how can she be safe traveling?
This view is stated in al-Mukhtar and al-Muhit as the chosen position.
3
Understand the basis for change
The later scholars rely on the Quranic principle 'do not harm them' (Quran 65:6) and the custom of harm in their time. They argue that the original ruling's premise (safety) no longer holds.
This is not a rejection of the texts but an application of the maxim that rulings can change with circumstances.
4
Determine the operative fatwa
There is no single mufta bihi. Some delegate to the mufti's discretion (al-Bazzaziyyah), some prefer the later view (al-Mukhtar), and others (al-Fusul) follow al-Qadi Khan's view to consider each case based on potential harm.
The mufti must assess harm and benefit in light of fasad al-zaman.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وله السفر بها بعد أدائه في ظاهر الرواية. أي للزوج أن يسافر بها بعد أداء القدر المعجل شرطاً أو عرفاً، وليس لها الامتناع من ذلك، وكذا له ذلك إذا أدّى كل المهر معجلاً كان أو مؤجلاً. ذكر في «البحر»: أولاً إنه إذا أوفاها المعجل، فالفتوى على أنه يسافر بها، كما في «جامع الفصولين». ثم ذكر عن الفقيه أبي القاسم الصفار وأبي الليث: إنه ليس له السفر مطلقاً بلا رضاها؛ لفساد الزمان؛ لأنها لا تأمن على نفسها في منزلها، فكيف إذا خرجت؟ وصرَّحَ في «المختار» أن عليه الفتوى، وذكر في «المحيط»: إنه المختار، واختاره كثير من مشايخنا، كما في «الكافي». وفوَّضَ الأمر فيه إلى المفتي في «البَزّازيّة» حيث قال: بعد إيفاء المهر إذا أراد أن يخرجها من بلدها الى بلاد الغربة يمنعُ من ذلك؛ لأنّ الغريب يؤذى ويتضرر لفساد الزمان. كذا اختاره الفقيه وبه يفتي. وقال القاضي: قول الله: أَسْكُنُوهُنَّ مِنْ حَيْثُ سَكَتُم أولى من قول الفقيه. قيل: قوله: وَلَا تُضَارُوهُنَّ في آخره دليل قول الفقيه؛ لأنـا قـد عادة زماننا مضارة قطيعة في الاغتراب بها. واختار في «الفصول» قول القاضي، فيفي بما يقع عنده من المضارة وعدمها؛ لأن المفتي إنما يفتي بحسب ما يقع عنده من المصلحة. وقيل: لا، وبه أفتى الفقيه أبو الليث، وله ذلك فيما دون مدته: أي له نقلها فيما دون مدَّةِ السِّفر.
And he has the right to travel with her after its payment in the apparent narration. That is, the husband may travel with her after paying the amount that is expedited by condition or custom, and she does not have the right to refuse that. Similarly, he may do so if he pays the entire mahr, whether it was immediate or deferred. It is mentioned in al-Bahr: first, if he pays her the expedited portion, the fatwa is that he may travel with her, as in Jami' al-Fusulayn. Then it is mentioned from al-Faqih Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar and Abu al-Layth that he does not have the right to travel at all without her consent due to the corruption of the time, because she is not secure in her own home, so how when she goes out? It is stated in al-Mukhtar that the fatwa is upon it, and in al-Muhit it is the chosen view, and many of our scholars chose it, as in al-Kafi. And in al-Bazzaziyyah, the matter is delegated to the mufti, where it says: after paying the mahr, if he wants to take her out of her town to foreign lands, he is prevented from that because the stranger is harmed and distressed due to the corruption of the time. So al-Faqih chose it and gives fatwa accordingly. And al-Qadi said: The word of Allah: 'Lodge them where you lodge' is more appropriate than the word of al-Faqih. It is said: His word: 'And do not harm them' later is evidence for the word of al-Faqih because our time's custom is pure harm in taking her abroad. And al-Fusul chose the word of al-Qadi, so he gives fatwa according to what occurs to him of harm or lack thereof, because the mufti only gives fatwa according to what occurs to him of benefit. And it is said: no, and al-Faqih Abu al-Layth gave fatwa accordingly. And he has that within its duration: i.e., he has the right to transfer her within the duration of travel.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the husband's right to travel with his wife after paying the mahr. The base text (matn) from al-Wiqayah states that according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), the husband may travel with her after payment. The commentator expands on this, explaining that this applies after paying the amount expedited by condition or custom, and also if the full mahr is paid. However, later Hanafi scholars differed. The first opinion, from al-Faqih Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar and Abu al-Layth, holds that he may not travel at all without her consent due to the corruption of the times (fasad al-zaman). This view is said to be the fatwa in al-Mukhtar and chosen by many scholars. A second opinion delegates the matter to the mufti, as in al-Bazzaziyyah: if taking her to foreign lands causes harm, it is prevented. A third opinion, from al-Qadi (likely al-Qadi al-Khan), prefers the Quranic command to lodge wives properly over the Faqih's view, and this is chosen in al-Fusul. Finally, some scholars allow travel within the duration of short trips (i.e., less than the travel distance of three days). The passage illustrates the dynamic nature of Hanafi fiqh, where later scholars may adjust rulings based on changing circumstances (fasad al-zaman).

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (zāhir al-riwāyah): The apparent or well-known transmission from the founding imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), as recorded in the six core books of Imam Muhammad (Zahir al-Riwayah).
فساد الزمان (fasād al-zamān): The corruption or moral decay of the time period, which may affect the applicability of certain legal rulings.
المفتى به (al-muftā bihi): The relied-upon position for issuing fatwas, often determined by later scholars considering evidence and circumstances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the later Hanafi scholars' view that the husband cannot travel with his wife without her consent?
A) The wife's right to receive the full mahr before travel
B) The corruption of the time (fasad al-zaman) and potential harm to the wife
C) The husband's lack of financial capability
D) The necessity of the wife's family's permission

Key Takeaway
The husband's right to travel with his wife after mahr payment is contested: the original ruling permits it, but later scholars restrict it due to fasad al-zaman, making the fatwa dependent on circumstances and mufti's discretion.

Classification of Mahr Disputes
Classification of mahr disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify disputes about mahr (dower) into two primary categories (amount vs. existence) and identify the subcategories based on the parties' status (alive/dead) and consummation (before/after).

Core Idea
Mahr disputes divide into amount (qadr) or existence (asl), each further split by life/death and consummation.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah sets out the taxonomy of mahr disputes. Before delving into detailed rulings, the commentator maps all possible scenarios. Understanding this classification is essential because the ruling changes depending on the type of dispute and the circumstances. We will parse the text to extract the legal categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two primary categories
The passage states that the dispute is either about the amount (qadr) of the mahr or about its existence (asl). Identify these two as the root divisions.
These are mutually exclusive: either the couple agrees that some mahr was fixed but disagrees on how much, or they disagree on whether any mahr was agreed upon at all.
2
Identify the temporal subcategories
Each primary category can occur while both spouses are alive, after both have died (dispute between heirs), or after one has died (dispute between the living spouse and the deceased's heirs). Recognize these as sub-categories based on who is disputing.
This affects who bears the burden of proof and which party claims.
3
Identify the effect of consummation
Each of the above scenarios is further conditioned on whether consummation (dukhūl) has taken place. Note that the text says 'after consummation or before it' for each scenario.
Consummation changes the obligation: full mahr becomes due after dukhūl, half mahr if divorce occurs before dukhūl.
4
Recognize the passage as an introduction
The passage ends by stating that the ruling for each scenario will come in detail later. This means the current text is purely a parsing exercise, setting up the branches for subsequent fiqh rulings.
The commentator's method is to first fully classify the subject before applying legal rules.

And if they differ regarding the mahr: i.e., if disagreement occurs between the spouses, and it is of several types: either it is about its amount, such as the woman claiming an increase and the husband denying, or about its existence, and each of these is either during their lifetimes, or after their deaths by disagreement between their heirs, or after the death of one of them by disagreement between the heirs of one and the other, and each of these is either after consummation or before it. Commentary
This passage introduces the legal classification of disputes between spouses concerning the mahr (dower). The commentator breaks down the possible scenarios: (1) dispute about the amount (e.g., wife claims a higher mahr than husband admits), (2) dispute about whether any mahr was fixed at all. Each of these can occur: (a) while both are alive, (b) after both have died, involving their heirs, (c) after one spouse dies, involving the living spouse and the deceased's heirs. Additionally, these disputes are further categorized based on whether consummation (dakhul) has taken place or not. The passage sets the stage for detailed rulings that follow later in the text. This is typical of Hanafi fiqh works: first parsing the subject into all its branches, then providing the ruling for each branch.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): The dower or bridal gift given by the husband to the wife as an obligation of the marriage contract.
الدخول (al-dukhūl): Consummation of the marriage, i.e., valid seclusion and sexual intercourse.

Key Takeaway
Disputes about mahr are classified first by subject (amount or existence), then by circumstances (life/death, consummation), and each scenario has a distinct ruling in Hanafi fiqh.

Three Hanafi Opinions on Traveling with Wife After Mahr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on husband's travel with wife after mahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three Hanafi opinions regarding a husband traveling with his wife after paying her mahr and identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling).

Core Idea
After paying mahr, the husband's right to travel with his wife is disputed: Zahir al-Riwayah permits it, but the relied-upon fatwa requires her consent.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether a husband can travel with his wife after fully paying her mahr. The passage presents three positions: one from the authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah, a second from later jurists who forbid travel without consent, and a third that leaves the matter to the mufti. Understanding this dispute reveals how the Hanafi school navigates between textual authority and practical considerations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The core question: after the husband has paid the full mahr, does he have the right to travel with his wife without her permission?
The mahr is a marital gift; its payment is a condition for full consummation rights.
2
State the First Opinion (Zahir al-Riwayah)
The apparent narration allows travel, provided the husband is trustworthy. This is the position of al-Marghinani and others.
This view is based on the general authority of the husband in marital relations.
3
State the Second Opinion (Abu al-Layth et al.)
Travel is absolutely prohibited without the wife's consent, because a stranger is degraded by such travel (al-gharib yumtahan). This is the mufta bihi in later texts.
This opinion gives weight to the wife's dignity and potential harm.
4
State the Third Opinion (Delegation to Mufti)
Some scholars leave the decision to the mufti's discretion, implying that circumstances may affect the ruling.
This reflects a cautious approach when the evidence is balanced.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
According to al-Mukhtar, al-Ghurar, and al-Multaqa, the relied-upon fatwa is the second opinion: no travel without the wife's consent.
Later authority tips the scale toward the wife's protection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيل : لا ، وبه أفتى الفقيه أبو الليث، وله ذلك فيما دون مدته أو قَدْرَ ما يُعَجَّلُ لمثلها في ظاهر الرواية ، وقيل : لا ، وبه أفتى الفقيه أبو الليث ، وله ذلك فيما دون مُدتِه : أي له نقلُها فيما دون مدَّةِ السِّفر. اختلفوا في أنه هل له السفر بها بعد أداء مهرها على أقوال : الأول: أنه له السفر بها، وهو ظاهر الرواية، واختاره ظهير الدين المرغيناني، وفي «التجنيس»: الفتوى عليه وبه أفتى صاحب ملتقى البحار»، واختاره صاحب «التنوير» واشترطا أن يكون الزوج مأموناً. الثاني : ليس له السفر بها مطلقاً دون رضاها ؛ لأن الغريب يمتهن، وبه أفتى أبو الليث، ومحمد ابن سلمة، واختاره أبو القاسم الصفار، وفي المختار، والغرر، والملتقى : عليه الفتوى. الثالث : تفويض الأمر فيه إلى المفتي، واختاره صاحب البزازية، وابن عابدين في رد المحتار.
And it was said: No, and by it gave fatwa the jurist Abu al-Layth, and he has that within less than its duration or the amount expedited for the like in the apparent narration, and it was said: No, and by it gave fatwa the jurist Abu al-Layth, and he has that within less than its duration: i.e., he may transfer her within less than the distance of travel. They differed concerning whether he may travel with her after paying her mahr, on several opinions: The first: that he may travel with her, and that is the apparent narration, and it was chosen by Zahir al-Din al-Marghinani, and in al-Tajnis: the fatwa is upon it, and by it gave fatwa the author of Multaqa al-Bihar, and it was chosen by the author of al-Tanwir, and they stipulated that the husband be trustworthy. The second: He may not travel with her at all without her consent, because the stranger is degraded, and by it gave fatwa Abu al-Layth and Muhammad ibn Salama, and it was chosen by Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar, and in al-Mukhtar, al-Ghurar, and al-Multaqa: the fatwa is upon it. The third: Delegation of the matter to the mufti, and it was chosen by the author of al-Bazzaziyya and Ibn Abidin in Radd al-Muhtar.
Source pages p. 156

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a husband may travel with his wife after fully paying her mahr. The commentary expands on the base text's ruling, noting that the apparent narration (Zahir al-Riwayah) permits it, as chosen by Al-Marghinani and others, with the condition that the husband is trustworthy. A second opinion, championed by Abu al-Layth and Muhammad ibn Salama, absolutely forbids it without her consent, arguing that a stranger is degraded. A third opinion leaves the decision to the mufti's discretion, as chosen by later scholars like the author of al-Bazzaziyya and Ibn Abidin.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The apparent or well-known narration from the school's founding texts, considered authoritative.
الفتوى عليه (al-fatwa 'alayh): The ruling upon which fatwa is given, indicating the relied-upon position.
مأمون (ma'mun): Trustworthy, reliable, especially in matters of honor and safety.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Although the Zahir al-Riwayah permits travel, the later Hanafi mufta bihi requires the wife's consent, protecting her dignity.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Swearing in Mahr Specification
Intra-Hanafi dispute on swearing in mahr disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on swearing in mahr disputes and explain the mufta bihi position with reasoning.

Core Idea
When spouses dispute mahr specification, the Sahibayn swear the denier; Abu Hanifa does not — the dispute turns on whether nukul is admission in marriage.

In Hanafi fiqh, if spouses disagree on whether a mahr was specified, the default is mahr al-mithl. However, a procedural question arises: should the judge administer an oath to the denier? This lesson unpacks the intra-Hanafi debate between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, and why later scholars preferred the view of the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute and its context
Recognise that the disagreement occurs when one spouse claims a mahr was specified (tasmiya) and the other denies it, and no evidence is produced. The underlying issue is whether to administer an oath (tahlif) to the denier.
2
State the position of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the denier should be sworn. If he refuses (nukul), that refusal is treated as an admission, establishing the claimed specification. If he swears, the claim fails and mahr al-mithl applies.
This is based on the general rule: al-bayyina 'ala al-mudda'i wa al-yamin 'ala man ankara.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa holds that no oath should be administered in marriage matters. According to him, nukul is not equivalent to admission in marriage (nikah) because marriage is not a financial transaction where badl (payment) applies. Thus, mahr al-mithl is directly imposed without swearing.
Abu Hanifa's reasoning: nukul is badl, not iqrar, and badl does not apply to marriage.
4
Analyse the legal reasoning behind each view
The Sahibayn consider the oath a standard procedural tool for any disputed claim, including mahr. Abu Hanifa restricts it because he views marriage as distinct from financial contracts. The key concept is whether nukul constitutes admission (iqrar) or payment (badl).
Remember: the dispute is procedural, not about the obligation of mahr al-mithl itself (which is agreed).
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the reason for tarjih
Later scholars (Mulla Khusraw, Ibn Kamal Pasha, etc.) clarified that the swearing here is about the mahr (money), not the marriage contract. Since swearing about money is permitted by consensus, the Sahibayn's view is mufta bihi. The initial claim of 'ijma on not swearing in marriage' was a leniency (musamaha) from the commentator.
Thus, in practice, the judge administers an oath to the denier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح باب المهر
ففي أصله : يجب مهر المثل إجماعاً
ففي أصله : يجب مهر المثل إجماعاً ) : أي إن اختلفا في المهر ، فقال : أحدهما لم يسم مهر ، وقال الآخر : قد سُمِّي ، فإن أقامَ البيِّنة فلا شك في قبولها، وإن لم يقم، فعندهما يحلف " ، فإن نَكَل يثبت دعوى التسمية، وإن حلف يجب مهر المثل، وأما عند أبي حنيفة ، ينبغي أن لا يُحَلِّفُ ) ؛ لأنَّه لا يُحَلِّفُ فِي النكاح، فيجب مهر المثل. [١]قوله : إجماعاً ؛ أي اتفاقاً بين أئمتنا ؛ لأنه تعذر القضاء بالمسمى لوقوع الشك في وجوده، فيصار إلى مهر المثل رفعاً للنزاع ، فإنّه إنما يتركُ لقوة المسمى، وإذ لم يثبت يلزم الرجوع إليه.
[٢] قوله : فإن أقام ؛ أي فإن أقامَ المدَّعي - وهو من يدعي التسمية – الشهود لإثبات دعواه تقبل ويثبت ما ادعاه، فيجب هو.
[٣]قوله : يحلف ؛ أي منكر التسمية، فإنَّ البَيِّنةَ على المدعي وعند عدمها اليمين على من أنكر، فيحلفه القاضي على إنكار التسمية. [٤]قوله : فإن نكل ؛ النكولُ : هو الإعراض عن الحلف : أي فإن لم يحلف ثَبَتَ دعوى التسمية ؛ لأن نكول المنكر في حكم الإقرار بما يدعي المدعي. [0] قوله : وإن حلف ؛ أي حَلَفَ المنكرُ على عدم التسمية، فحينئذ يبطل دعوى المدعي، ولا تثبت التسمية، وفيما لا تسمية فيه يجب مهر المثل كما مرّ. [٦] قوله : وأما عند أبي حنيفة الله ؛ حاصله : إن التحليف في هذه المسألة إنما هو على قول أبي يوسف ومحمد ، وأما عند أبي حنيفة : فلا يحلف ؛ لأن النكول عنده ليس في حكم الإقرار، بل هو بذل، فلا يحلفُ فيما لا يجري فيه البذل : كالنكاح والرجعة على ما سيأتي تفصيله في موضعه إن شاء الله تعالى.
فعنده إن أقام مدعي التسمية البيَّنةَ قُبِلَت ، وإن لم يُقِم يُحْكَمُ بمهر المثل، وهذا
(۱) هذه من مسامحات الشارح رحمه الله وقد نبه عليه من جاء بعده كملا خسرو في «درر الحكام»(۱ : ٣٤٧، وابن كمال باشا في الايضاح ( ق ٤٨ /أ) ، وابن نجيم في «البحر»(۳: ۱۹۷)، وابن عابدين في منحة الخالق (۳): ۱۹۷ وغيرهم ؛ لأن التحليف هنا على المهر لا على أصل النكاح، وفيها الحلف بالاجماع.
Book of Nikah, Chapter of Mahr. In its origin: mahr al-mithl is obligatory by consensus. In its origin: mahr al-mithl is obligatory by consensus): meaning if they differ about the mahr, one said: he did not specify a mahr, and the other said: it was specified. If he produces evidence, there is no doubt about accepting it. If he does not produce evidence, then according to them (Sahibayn) he is made to swear. If he refuses (nukul), the claim of specification is established. If he swears, mahr al-mithl is obligatory. As for Abu Hanifa, it is appropriate not to make him swear; because he does not make anyone swear in marriage, so mahr al-mithl is obligatory. [1] His saying: 'by consensus'; meaning agreement among our imams; because ruling by the specified amount is impossible due to doubt about its existence, so recourse is had to mahr al-mithl to remove the dispute; for it (specified amount) is only left due to the strength of the specified, and when it is not proven, recourse to it becomes necessary. [2] His saying: 'if he produces evidence'; meaning if the claimant - who is the one claiming specification - produces witnesses to prove his claim, it is accepted and his claim is established, so the specified mahr becomes obligatory. [3] His saying: 'he swears'; meaning the denier of specification; for evidence is on the claimant, and in its absence, the oath is on the denier, so the judge makes him swear on the denial of specification. [4] His saying: 'if he refuses'; nukul is turning away from the oath: meaning if he does not swear, the claim of specification is established; because the refusal of the denier is considered as an admission of what the claimant claims. [5] His saying: 'and if he swears'; meaning the denier swears on the absence of specification, then the claimant's claim is invalidated and specification is not established; and where there is no specification, mahr al-mithl is obligatory as previously mentioned. [6] His saying: 'and as for Abu Hanifa'; its gist: that making the denier swear in this issue is according to the saying of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. As for Abu Hanifa, he does not make him swear; because nukul according to him is not considered an admission, rather it is a payment (badhl), so he does not make anyone swear in matters where payment does not apply: such as marriage and revocation (raj'a), as will come in detail in its place if Allah wills. According to him, if the claimant of specification produces evidence, it is accepted; if he does not produce evidence, judgment is given for mahr al-mithl. And this (1) is from the leniencies of the commentator, may Allah have mercy on him, and those who came after him pointed it out, such as Mulla Khusraw in Durar al-Hukkam (1:347), Ibn Kamal Pasha in al-Idah (folio 48/a), Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr (3:197), Ibn Abidin in Minhat al-Khaliq (3:197), and others; because the swearing here is about the mahr, not about the marriage itself, and swearing occurs in it by consensus.
Source pages p. 157

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the procedure when spouses disagree about whether a mahr was specified (tasmia) at the time of marriage. The commentator explains that there is consensus (ijma) among the Hanafi imams that if the existence of a specified mahr cannot be proven, then mahr al-mithl is obligatory. The dispute arises when one spouse claims a mahr was specified and the other denies it, and no evidence is produced. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), the denier is made to swear an oath. If he refuses (nukul), that refusal is treated as an admission, and the claim of specification is established, so the specified mahr becomes due. If he swears, the claim fails, and mahr al-mithl is obligatory. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, holds that no oath is administered in matters of marriage (nikah) because nukul in his view is not equivalent to admission but rather a 'badhl' (payment) that does not apply to marriage. Therefore, according to Abu Hanifa, if the claimant produces evidence, it is accepted; otherwise, mahr al-mithl is directly imposed without swearing. The commentator notes that the statement about consensus on not swearing in marriage is a leniency (musamaha) from the original commentator, as later scholars clarified that the swearing here is about the mahr (money) not the marriage contract itself, and swearing about money is permissible even according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
مهر المثل (mahr al-mithl): The mahr that is appropriate for a woman similar to her in status, family, and circumstance, used when no specific mahr is agreed or proven.
تسمية المهر (tasmiyat al-mahr): The specification of a mahr at the time of marriage contract, whether verbal or written.
نكول (nukul): Refusal to take an oath; in legal context, it is treated as an admission of the opponent's claim according to the Sahibayn, but not according to Abu Hanifa in marriage matters.
تحليف (tahlif): Administration of an oath by the judge to a party in a dispute.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why is the denier not made to swear when spouses dispute the specification of mahr?
A) Because nukul is considered an admission only in financial matters.
B) Because nukul is not considered an admission in marriage matters, and marriage is not a financial transaction where badl applies.
C) Because the claimant has the burden of proof and cannot compel an oath.
D) Because the judge cannot administer oaths in marriage disputes.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school for mahr specification disputes is the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani: the denier is sworn, and nukul establishes the claim.
